2:45:3416:0:14:72:508:700:12:Times:12:Times:?:Liquidity vs. Wealth in Household Debt Obligations: Evidence from Housing Policy in the
2:46:3503:14:14:72:150:686:12:Times:12:Times:?:Great Recession
2:47:3518:14:14:72:218:672:12:Times:12:Times:?:Peter Ganong and Pascal Noel
2:48:3546:14:14:72:234:658:12:Times:12:Times:?:NBER Working Paper No. 24964
2:49:3574:14:14:72:134:644:12:Times:12:Times:?:August 2018
2:50:3585:14:28:72:182:630:12:Times:12:Times:?:JEL No. D14,G21,R28
2:51:3604:28:28:273:338:602:12:Times:12:Times:?:ABSTRACT
2:52:3612:28:14:72:546:574:12:Times:12:Times:?:We  use  variation  in  mortgage  modifications  to  disentangle  the  impact  of  reducing  long-term 
2:53:3715:14:14:72:545:560:12:Times:12:Times:?:obligations with no change in short-term payments (“wealth”), and reducing short-term payments 
2:54:3809:14:14:72:546:546:12:Times:12:Times:?:with   approximately no   change   in   long-term   obligations   (“liquidity”).   Using   regression 
2:55:3910:14:14:72:545:532:12:Times:12:Times:?:discontinuity  and  difference-in-differences research  designs  with  administrative  data  measuring 
2:56:4012:14:14:72:546:518:12:Times:12:Times:?:default  and  consumption,  we  find  that  principal reductions  that  increase  housing  wealth  without 
2:57:4118:14:14:72:546:504:12:Times:12:Times:?:affecting  liquidity  have  no  effect,  while  maturity  extensions that  increase  only  liquidity  have 
2:58:4224:14:14:72:546:490:12:Times:12:Times:?:large  effects.  Our  results  suggest  that  liquidity  drives  borrower  default and  consumption 
2:59:4323:14:14:72:545:476:12:Times:12:Times:?:decisions,  and  that  distressed  debt  restructurings  can  be  redesigned  with  substantial gains  to 
2:60:4428:14:42:72:237:462:12:Times:12:Times:?:borrowers, lenders, and taxpayers.
2:61:4462:42:14:72:138:420:12:Times:12:Times:?:Peter Ganong
2:62:4474:14:14:72:219:406:12:Times:12:Times:?:Harris School of Public Policy
2:63:4504:14:14:72:179:392:12:Times:12:Times:?:University of Chicago
2:64:4525:14:14:72:165:378:12:Times:12:Times:?:1155 E. 60th Street

2:74:4716:166:0:72:449:72:12:Times:12:Times:?:An online appendix is available at http://www.nber.org/data-appendix/w24964
3:75:4791:0:31:89:202:709:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:1  Introduction
3:76:4806:31:16:106:523:678:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Record foreclosure rates and reduced aggregate demand during the Great Recession
3:77:4886:16:16:89:522:662:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sparked a vigorous policy debate about how to decrease defaults and increase consumption
3:78:4974:16:17:89:522:646:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of struggling borrowers. Former Treasury Secretary Timothy Geithner has explained that
3:79:5060:17:16:89:522:629:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the government’s “biggest debate was whether to try to reduce overall mortgage loans or
3:80:5147:16:17:89:522:613:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:just monthly payments” (Geithner 2014). A wide range of economists have argued that
3:81:5230:17:16:89:522:596:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:failing to address debt levels by permanently forgiving mortgage principal was a missed
3:82:5317:16:17:89:522:580:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:opportunity and one of the biggest policy mistakes of the Great Recession.1Others have
3:83:5403:17:16:89:522:563:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:argued instead that if borrowers are liquidity constrained, focusing on short-term payment
3:84:5493:16:16:89:411:547:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reductions is more cost e-ective (Eberly and Krishnamurthy 2014).
3:85:5558:16:17:106:523:531:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The normative policy debate hinges on fundamental economic questions about the rel-
3:86:5641:17:16:89:523:514:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ative e-ect of short- vs long-term debt obligations. For default, the underlying question
3:87:5730:16:17:89:522:498:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:is whether it is primarily driven by a lack of cash to make payments in the short-term or
3:88:5819:17:16:89:522:481:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:whether it is a response to the total burden of long-term debt obligations, sometimes known
3:89:5910:16:17:89:522:465:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:as “strategic default.”  For consumption, the underlying question is whether underwater
3:90:5997:17:16:89:522:448:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers have a high marginal propensity to consume (MPC) out of either changes in total
3:91:6086:16:17:89:522:432:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:housing wealth or changes in immediate cash-flow.2A broad literature evaluates the e-ects
3:92:6175:17:16:89:522:415:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of changes in debt obligations that simultaneously reduce both short-term and long-term
3:93:6262:16:16:89:522:399:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payments and consistently shows that debt obligations matter.3Reducing payments leads
3:94:6347:16:17:89:522:383:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to decreased defaults and increased consumption. However, to fully understand the e-ect of
3:95:6437:17:16:89:522:366:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:debt on borrower decisions and to inform the debate about liquidity- versus wealth-focused
3:96:6527:16:17:89:523:350:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:interventions, it is essential to separately estimate the e-ect of short-term and long-term
3:97:6618:17:16:89:166:333:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:debt reductions.
3:98:6634:16:17:106:523:317:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We fill this void by exploiting two natural experiments to separately identify the impact
3:99:6723:17:16:89:522:300:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of reducing long-term obligations without changing short-term payments (“wealth”), and
3:100:6809:16:16:89:521:284:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reducing short-term payments without changing long-term obligations (“liquidity”).We
3:101:6893:16:17:89:522:268:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:find that mortgage principal reduction that increases housing wealth without a-ecting liq-
3:102:6983:17:16:89:522:251:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:uidity has no significant impact on default or consumption for underwater borrowers. In
3:103:7070:16:17:89:522:235:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:contrast, we show that maturity extension, which immediately reduces payments but leaves
3:104:7158:17:16:89:521:218:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:long-term obligations approximately unchanged, does significantly reduce default rates.4
3:105:7246:16:17:89:522:202:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Taken together, these results suggest that liquidity is the key driver of borrower default and
3:106:7340:17:16:89:522:185:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:consumption decisions. Furthermore, we show that this lesson can be used to inform the
3:107:7426:16:16:89:523:169:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:e-cient design of distressed debt restructurings, with the potential for substantial gains to
3:108:7519:16:15:101:522:153:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:1See Goldfarb (2012) for a review of the academic support for principal reductions. Geanakoplos and
3:109:7618:15:11:89:522:138:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:Koniak (2009) argued that a plan to reduce payments and leave principal unchanged “wastes taxpayer
3:110:7716:11:7:89:511:127:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:money and won’t fix the problem.” See also Feldstein (2009), Romer (2011), and Mian and Sufi (2014b).
3:111:7817:7:11:101:517:120:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:?:2An “underwater” or negative equity borrower owes more on their home than its current market value.
3:112:7916:11:15:101:522:109:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:3See Agarwal et al. (2017a), Agarwal et al. (2017b), Abel and Fuster (2018), DiMaggio et al. (2017),
3:113:8016:15:7:89:424:94:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:Ehrlich and Perry (2015), Fuster and Willen (2017), and Tracy and Wright (2016).
3:114:8096:7:15:101:522:87:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:4Although our research designs are underpowered for estimating the causal e-ect of payment reductions
3:115:8197:15:0:89:480:72:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:on consumption, we provide suggestive evidence that payment reductions also increase spending.
4:116:8292:0:17:89:252:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers, lenders, and taxpayers.
4:117:8326:17:16:106:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our first natural experiment allows us to isolate the e-ect of wealth by comparing under-
4:118:8415:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:water borrowers who receive two types of modifications in the federal government’s Home
4:119:8502:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:A-ordable Modification Program (HAMP). Both modification types result in identical pay-
4:120:8589:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ment reductions for the first five years.  However, one group also receives an average of
4:121:8678:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:$67,000 in mortgage principal forgiveness, which translates into long-term payment relief.
4:122:8768:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Because borrowers remain slightly underwater even after substantial principal forgiveness,
4:123:8858:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:their short-term access to liquidity is unchanged. By exploiting quasi-experimental assign-
4:124:8949:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ment of borrowers to each of these modification types, we isolate the e-ects of long-term
4:125:9038:16:17:89:305:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:debt levels holding fixed short-term liquidity.
4:126:9085:17:16:106:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our second natural experiment exploits an eligibility cuto-rule for HAMP that gen-
4:127:9167:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:erates the opposite treatment: an increase in liquidity with approximately no change in
4:128:9254:17:16:89:523:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:wealth. Borrowers above the cuto-receive small payment reductions from HAMP while
4:129:9335:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers below the cuto-are ineligible for the government program but receive larger
4:130:9420:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payment reductions through alternative private sector modifications. Government program
4:131:9507:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rules prohibit the private sector from o-ering these alternative modifications to eligible bor-
4:132:9602:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rowers above the cuto-under the (erroneous) assumption that the government-subsidized
4:133:9687:17:16:89:523:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications would always be more e-ective.  The private sector finances these deeper
4:134:9773:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payment reductions by first extending mortgage maturities prior to additional modification
4:135:9863:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:steps, such that larger immediate payment reductions are o-set by continued payments in
4:136:9950:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the long term. This restructuring leaves the net present value of total mortgage payments
4:137:10039:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:owed approximately unchanged. By comparing borrowers on either side of this cuto-we
4:138:10122:16:16:89:476:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:isolate the e-ect of immediate liquidity provision holding fixed long-term wealth.
4:139:10204:16:17:106:523:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:To study these natural experiments we build two new datasets with information on
4:140:10284:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrower outcomes and program participation. Our first dataset matches administrative
4:141:10369:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:data on HAMP participants to monthly consumer credit bureau records. We exploit detailed
4:142:10457:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:account-level information to construct a novel measure of consumer spending based on
4:143:10541:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:monthly credit card expenditures.  We also followDiMaggio et al. (2017)by using new
4:144:10624:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:auto loan originations as a proxy for durable consumption. Our second dataset uses de-
4:145:10710:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:identified mortgage and credit card data from the JPMorgan Chase Institute (JPMCI).It
4:146:10795:17:16:89:522:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:includes monthly information on all borrowers whose mortgages are serviced by Chase and
4:147:10882:16:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:who receive either a government-subsidized modification through HAMP or an alternative
4:148:10968:16:17:89:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:private modification. Our samples from both datasets are similar on observable borrower
4:149:11055:17:16:89:160:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:characteristics.
4:150:11071:16:17:106:523:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our empirical analysis proceeds in three steps. First, we estimate the causal impact of
4:151:11158:17:16:89:522:133:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction on default by exploiting a cuto-rule in borrower assignment to the two
4:152:11248:16:17:89:522:117:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP modification types. Mortgage servicers evaluated underwater applicants for both
4:153:11332:17:16:89:522:100:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification types by calculating the expected gain to investors under either option using
4:154:11422:16:0:89:522:84:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a standard government-supplied formula. There is a sharp 41 percentage point jump in the
5:155:11511:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:probability that a borrower receives principal reduction when the calculation shows that
5:156:11599:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction is marginally more beneficial to investors. We exploit this jump with a
5:157:11690:16:17:89:488:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:regression discontinuity estimator comparing borrowers on either side of this cuto-.
5:158:11774:17:16:106:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We find that principal reduction has no e-ect on default. Despite a $30,000 increase in
5:159:11861:16:17:89:523:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal forgiveness in the treatment group at the cuto-(translating to an 11 percentage
5:160:11950:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:point reduction in a borrower’s loan-to-value ratio), default rates are unchanged. We calcu-
5:161:12042:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:late that even at the upper bound of our confidence interval, the government spent $556,000
5:162:12133:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:per avoided foreclosure. This cost is over an order of magnitude greater than estimates of
5:163:12223:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the social cost of foreclosures (U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development 2010).
5:164:12311:16:17:106:523:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In the second step of our empirical analysis we examine the causal impact of principal
5:165:12397:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction on consumption. Our preferred empirical strategy for analyzing consumption is
5:166:12484:16:17:89:523:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a panel di-erence-in-di-erences estimator which is more precise than our regression discon-
5:167:12575:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:tinuity strategy.5We compare HAMP borrowers who receive principal reductions to other
5:168:12660:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP borrowers who receive only payment reductions. We find that an average of $67,000
5:169:12746:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in principal reduction has no significant impact on underwater borrowers’ credit card or auto
5:170:12839:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:expenditure. Translating our results into an annual MPC for total consumption, our point
5:171:12927:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:estimate is that borrowers increased consumption by three-tenths of one cent per dollar of
5:172:13017:17:16:89:419:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction, with an upper bound of eight-tenths of one cent.
5:173:13086:16:17:106:523:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In the third step of our empirical analysis we estimate the causal impact of immediate
5:174:13172:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payment reductions on default.  This analysis exploits HAMP’s eligibility cuto-using a
5:175:13258:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:regression discontinuity design.  There is an 18 percentage point jump in the amount of
5:176:13345:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payment reduction received by borrowers with private modifications just below the cut-
5:177:13431:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:o-. Although there is a large change in immediate liquidity at the cuto-, because these
5:178:13518:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:deeper payment reductions are largely financed by extending mortgage maturities there is
5:179:13606:17:16:89:472:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:no significant change in the net present value of total long-term payments owed.
5:180:13686:16:17:106:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In contrast to our results on the ine-ectiveness of principal reduction, we find that
5:181:13771:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:immediate payment reduction significantly reduces default rates. Default rates fall sharply
5:182:13862:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:by six percentage points at the cuto-from a control mean of 32 percentage points, implying
5:183:13952:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that a one percent payment reduction reduces default rates by about one percent. While
5:184:14038:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:our data and available research designs are unsuited for credibly estimating the causal e-ect
5:185:14131:17:16:89:522:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of immediate payment reduction on consumption, we provide suggestive evidence from the
5:186:14217:16:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:timeseries pattern of spending around modification that spending also rises when monthly
5:187:14305:16:17:89:156:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payments fall.
5:188:14319:17:16:106:523:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Combining the three steps of our empirical analysis, the central contribution of this paper
5:189:14410:16:17:89:522:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:is to disentangle the e-ects of liquidity and wealth on mortgagor outcomes. Disentangling
5:190:14499:17:16:89:522:133:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:these e-ects allows us to draw two types of lessons. First, from a positive perspective, we
5:191:14590:16:16:89:522:117:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:shed light on the mechanisms underlying the previously-documented relationships between
5:192:14677:16:15:101:522:101:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:5We also report estimates from the regression discontinuity design and show that this strategy is statis-
5:193:14782:15:0:89:398:86:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:tically and economically uninformative for analyzing consumption outcomes.
6:194:14857:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:housing wealth, housing debt, default, and consumption. Second, from a normative perspec-
6:195:14946:17:16:89:523:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:tive, we use these results to inform the debate about the e-cient structure of re-negotiations
6:196:15040:16:17:89:184:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:during a debt crisis.
6:197:15061:17:16:106:523:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:For default, we show that the strong cross-sectional relationship between leverage and
6:198:15147:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:default is not causal for underwater borrowers. Instead of borrowers defaulting for strategic
6:199:15240:17:16:89:521:626:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:reasons, we find that borrower default decisions are based primarily on immediate liquidity.6
6:200:15333:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:The cross-sectional evidence may have been misleading because borrowers with less equity
6:201:15421:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:purchased homes near the height of the credit boom and were less creditworthy on other
6:202:15507:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:dimensions (Palmer 2015), or because the large price reductions that left many borrowers
6:203:15595:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:underwater were also correlated with other omitted economic shocks that themselves could
6:204:15683:17:16:89:375:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:be responsible for higher default rates (Adelino et al. 2016).
6:205:15745:16:17:106:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:From a specific policy perspective, our default results suggest a significant ine-ciency
6:206:15833:17:16:89:523:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:at the HAMP eligibility cuto-.  The government spent substantial resources subsidizing
6:207:15919:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP modifications above the cuto-with small payment reductions and high default rates,
6:208:16006:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:whereas borrowers below the cuto-received private modifications requiring no government
6:209:16093:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:assistance, which had large payment reductions and low default rates.  In fact, there is
6:210:16181:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f6:B:likely a Pareto improvement for borrowers, lenders, and taxpayers from shifting the cuto-
6:211:16270:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:such that fewer borrowers receive HAMP and more borrowers receive private modifications.
6:212:16358:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:We find that 40 percent of HAMP borrowers are in the region where a private alternative,
6:213:16446:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:such as the one we study, would have provided deeper payment reductions and led to
6:214:16528:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduced default rates. Government rules prohibiting servicers from o-ering these private
6:215:16616:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:bilateral alternatives based on the assumption that proprietary modifications could not be
6:216:16706:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:as e-ective as those subsidized by the government may have crowded out more e-ective
6:217:16790:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications for these borrowers. Our finding that payment reductions can be structured
6:218:16878:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:so as to reduce default rates while leaving all parties better o-contrasts sharply with our
6:219:16969:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:finding for principal reduction, which was ine-ective for borrowers even while being costly
6:220:17060:17:16:89:235:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to both lenders and taxpayers.
6:221:17090:16:17:106:523:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:From a broader policy perspective, this lesson can be used to characterize the default-
6:222:17177:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:minimizing modification structure for all borrowers.  Since immediate liquidity provision
6:223:17266:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduces default rates but long-term wealth does not, the e-cient modification structure
6:224:17353:17:16:89:522:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:maximizes short-term liquidity provision, in the spirit of Eberly and Krishnamurthy (2014).
6:225:17444:16:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:We trace out the default-minimizing modification frontier and find the potential for sub-
6:226:17533:16:17:89:333:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:stantial gains to borrowers, lenders, and taxpayers.
6:227:17585:17:16:106:522:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We consider two ways to quantify the potential gains of more e-cient modifications
6:228:17667:16:17:89:522:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:relative to the type of restructurings previously pursued. First, we calculate that the median
6:229:17761:17:16:89:522:133:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:amount of payment reduction in HAMP could have been provided at a $63,000 lower cost
6:230:17845:16:17:89:522:117:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:per modification to lenders and taxpayers (a savings of 26 percent of the unpaid balance),
6:231:17935:17:14:101:522:100:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:6Our results are consistent with the default rate mechanically increasing once borrowers move from
6:232:18033:14:11:89:523:86:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:positive to negative equity, since this has a large negative liquidity e-ect. Above water borrowers can avoid
6:233:18142:11:0:89:456:75:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:default by selling their home or borrowing against their home (Gupta and Hansman 2018).
7:234:18230:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:translating to a total potential unnecessary cost of $108 billion aggregating over all HAMP
7:235:18321:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications. Alternatively, if modifications maximized the amount of payment reduction
7:236:18409:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:while holding costs fixed, it would have been possible to cut default rates by one-third,
7:237:18498:17:16:89:428:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:avoiding 240,000 defaults at no additional cost to lenders or taxpayers.
7:238:18570:16:17:106:523:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:For consumption, we show that the tight link between housing wealth and consumption
7:239:18653:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:breaks down when borrowers are underwater. Our estimated MPC out of housing wealth
7:240:18735:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:for underwater borrowers is an order of magnitude smaller than the MPC for average home-
7:241:18823:17:16:89:523:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:owners examined in prior studies.7Furthermore, prior research has found high-leverage
7:242:18908:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers appear to be even more responsive. Mian et al. (2013) find that households living
7:243:18999:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in zip codes with average loan-to-value (LTV) ratios above 90 have MPCs that are twice that
7:244:19090:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of the median household, translating into an MPC of 18 cents. This result has been used
7:245:19177:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:by policy advocates arguing in favor of principal reduction for underwater borrowers (Gold-
7:246:19268:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:farb 2012). However, our evidence suggests that borrowers who are far underwater have
7:247:19353:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:much lower MPCs out of housing wealth, rendering principal reductions for these borrowers
7:248:19442:17:16:89:139:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ine-ective.
7:249:19453:16:16:106:523:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We argue that the inability of underwater borrowers to monetize the wealth gains from
7:250:19538:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction can explain why they are far less sensitive to housing wealth changes than
7:251:19632:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers in other economic conditions. Typically, housing wealth gains expand borrowers’
7:252:19721:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:credit access (Mian and Sufi 2014a). But if homeowners face a collateral constraint, principal
7:253:19815:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction that still leaves borrowers underwater or nearly underwater will not immediately
7:254:19905:16:17:89:523:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:relax this constraint, which may explain why principal reduction is ine-ective. We develop
7:255:19995:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a partial-equilibrium life cycle model to formally analyze whether a delay in being able to
7:256:20086:16:16:89:523:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:access housing wealth can explain why consumption is una-ected by principal reduction.
7:257:20172:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:The model shows that collateral constraints drive a wedge between the MPC out of cash and
7:258:20261:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the MPC out of housing wealth for underwater borrowers. Thus, policies to increase housing
7:259:20351:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:wealth are unable to stimulate demand when borrowers are so far underwater that home
7:260:20435:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:equity gains fail to relax binding collateral constraints, which was precisely the situation
7:261:20527:16:17:89:270:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:when such policies were implemented.
7:262:20563:17:16:106:523:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:This paper contributes to several additional strands of the literature. Scharlemann and
7:263:20650:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Shore (2016) analyze principal reduction in HAMP using a regression kink design and also
7:264:20738:17:16:89:522:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:find that principal reduction is a costly way to reduce defaults. Relative to Scharlemann
7:265:20827:16:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and Shore (2016), our contributions are the introduction of a regression discontinuity design
7:266:20920:16:17:89:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that requires weaker parametric assumptions, an examination of the impact of principal
7:267:21006:17:16:89:522:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction on consumption and payment reduction on default, and the development of a
7:268:21089:16:16:89:522:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:model that clarifies the mechanisms causing principal reductions to be ine-ective.8Agarwal
7:269:21179:16:15:101:522:134:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:7See Aladangady (2017), Attanasio et al. (2009), Berger et al. (2018), Campbell and Cocco (2007), Carroll
7:270:21284:15:7:89:324:119:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:et al. (2011), Case et al. (2013), and Guren et al. (2018b).
7:271:21344:7:15:101:522:112:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:8Outside of mortgages, Dobbie and Song (2016) analyze future payment reductions for credit card bor-
7:272:21444:15:11:89:522:97:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:rowers. In contrast to our findings, they find that reducing future payments by 8 percent of the total debt
7:273:21551:11:11:89:522:86:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:owed leads to a reduction in short-term default of 1.6 percentage points. When scaled to to an equivalent
7:274:21656:11:0:89:522:75:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:treatment size, this is larger than our point estimate but within our confidence interval. One possible expla-
8:275:21767:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:et al. (2017a) study the overall e-ect of HAMP modifications, which combine both short-
8:276:21854:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:term and long-term payment reductions. We complement their findings by separating the
8:277:21939:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:e-ect of long-term from short-term payment reductions, providing evidence that short-
8:278:22024:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:term payment reductions are largely responsible for the program’s e-ects. This allows us
8:279:22112:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to identify the underlying mechanisms driving borrower responses to debt reductions and
8:280:22199:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:therefore to analyze the optimal structure of debt renegotiations. These empirical lessons
8:281:22289:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:about ex-post renegotiation also help inform a growing theoretical literature about optimal
8:282:22380:17:16:89:212:593:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:ex-ante mortgage design.9
8:283:22405:16:16:106:523:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our model also contributes to a new literature finding little direct linkage between
8:284:22489:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:debt levels and consumption when debt is modeled as a long-term contract (Kaplan et al.
8:285:22576:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:2017, Justiniano et al. 2015). This contrasts with debt overhang models in which forced
8:286:22663:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:deleveraging of short-term debt leads to depressed consumption during a credit crunch
8:287:22748:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:(Eggertsson and Krugman 2012, Guerrieri and Lorenzoni 2017). In our model, as in practice,
8:288:22838:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:nothing forces borrowers to immediately delever when they are far underwater, removing a
8:289:22926:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:mechanical link between debt levels and consumption present in some of the prior literature
8:290:23017:16:16:89:386:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and reducing the expected e-ectiveness of principal reduction.
8:291:23079:16:17:106:523:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The remainder of the paper is organized as follows. Section 2 describes the data. Sections
8:292:23169:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:3 and 4 analyze the e-ect of principal reduction on default and consumption, respectively.
8:293:23259:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Section 5 analyzes the e-ect of payment reduction on default.  Section 6 discusses the
8:294:23345:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:implications of our default results. Section 7 discusses the implications of our consumption
8:295:23437:16:25:89:256:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:results. The last section concludes.
8:296:23473:25:30:89:164:355:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:2Data
8:297:23478:30:16:106:523:325:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We use two datasets.  Our first dataset matches administrative HAMP participation
8:298:23559:16:17:89:522:309:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:data to consumer credit bureau records. This dataset covers a broad sample population
8:299:23644:17:16:89:522:292:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and allows us to carefully analyze the mechanisms assigning borrowers to each modification
8:300:23734:16:17:89:522:276:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:type in HAMP, which we exploit to estimate the impact of principal reduction. Our second
8:301:23822:17:16:89:522:259:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:dataset comes from a bank that is also a servicer that o-ers both government-subsidized
8:302:23909:16:17:89:522:243:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP modifications as well as private modifications. This allows us to analyze variation
8:303:23997:17:16:89:522:226:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in immediate payment reduction between public and private modifications and to examine
8:304:24083:16:20:89:231:210:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:administrative spending data.
8:305:24112:20:26:89:334:190:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:2.1  Matched HAMP Credit Bureau File
8:306:24148:26:17:106:523:164:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The U.S. Treasury releases a public data file on the universe of HAMP applicants.
8:307:24229:17:16:89:522:147:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:This loan-level dataset includes information on borrower characteristics and mortgage terms
8:308:24320:16:20:89:522:131:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:before and after modification.  Crucially, it also includes the NPV calculations run by
8:309:24407:20:11:89:522:111:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:nation is that borrowers behave more strategically with respect to credit card debt because the consequences
8:310:24515:11:7:89:453:100:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:of default are less severe than defaulting on a mortgage, which often results in foreclosure.
8:311:24608:7:15:101:522:93:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:9See Piskorski and Tchistyi (2010), Eberly and Krishnamurthy (2014), Guren et al. (2018a), Campbell
8:312:24707:15:0:89:259:78:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:et al. (2018), and Greenwald et al. (2018).
9:313:24751:0:17:89:392:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:servicers when evaluating borrowers for each modification type.
9:314:24814:17:16:106:523:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In order to observe a wide range of borrower outcomes, we use depersonalized consumer
9:315:24899:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:credit bureau records from TransUnion. HAMP program rules require servicers to report
9:316:24984:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrower participation to credit bureaus.  We use the universe of records for borrowers
9:317:25071:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:flagged as having received HAMP. We have monthly account-level information between
9:318:25153:17:16:89:340:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:January 2010 and December 2014 for each borrower.
9:319:25202:16:17:106:523:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We develop proxies for both durable and nondurable consumption based on the credit
9:320:25284:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:bureau records. For durable consumption, we follow DiMaggio et al. (2017) by using changes
9:321:25374:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in auto loan balances as a measure of car purchases. DiMaggio et al. (2017) document that
9:322:25463:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:leveraged car purchases account for 80 percent of total car sales. While prior work relied on
9:323:25556:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:observing jumps in total auto loan balances to infer new loans, our product account-level
9:324:25645:16:17:89:301:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:data allows us to observe new loans directly.
9:325:25690:17:16:106:523:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The detailed nature of our credit bureau data also allow us to construct a new measure
9:326:25776:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of consumption based on credit card expenditures.  In particular, we calculate monthly
9:327:25862:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:expenditures using end of month balances and payments made in a given month.10We are
9:328:25946:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:able to construct this measure for 83 percent of all credit and charge card accounts (not
9:329:26035:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:all servicers report monthly payments). We find average credit card spending of $425 per
9:330:26123:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:month in our sample, which is 80 percent of the average credit card spending per adult
9:331:26209:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in 2012 (Federal Reserve 2014), commensurate with the 83 percent of cards for which we
9:332:26295:17:16:89:192:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:observe expenditures.
9:333:26316:16:17:106:523:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We match borrowers in the HAMP dataset to their credit bureau records using loan and
9:334:26400:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrower attributes present in both files. The attributes we use are metro area, modification
9:335:26493:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:month, origination year, loan balance, and monthly payment before and after modification.
9:336:26582:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:When two borrowers are listed on a mortgage, we measure consumption using the credit
9:337:26666:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:bureau records of both borrowers. We are able to match half of the records in our sample
9:338:26754:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:window, resulting in a panel dataset of about 106,000 underwater households eligible for
9:339:26842:17:16:89:251:281:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:both HAMP modification types.11
9:340:26873:16:17:106:523:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The imperfect match rate does not bias our sample along any observed borrower char-
9:341:26956:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:acteristics. Online Appendix Table 1 reports summary statistics for our sample before and
9:342:27045:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:after the credit bureau match. This table shows that borrower characteristics are similar
9:343:27134:17:16:89:523:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in the matched sample. The final column shows that the di-erence in means for any char-
9:344:27221:16:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:acteristic is less than one-fifth of a standard deviation.  For our regression discontinuity
9:345:27313:16:15:98:522:183:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:10Letbtdenote the balance at the end of montht, andptbe the payment made in montht.We calculate
9:346:27408:15:11:89:522:168:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:expenditure in monthtaset=bt≠bt≠1+pt.Because interest rates and fees are not reported, we do not
9:347:27504:11:11:89:522:157:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:distinguish between new purchases, interest charges, and fees in this dataset. In the bank dataset described
9:348:27612:11:7:89:425:146:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:in Section 2.2 we can isolate purchases and confirm that our results are unchanged.
9:349:27695:7:14:98:522:139:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:11Our match rate is less than 100 percent due to rounding and changing reporting requirements. The
9:350:27793:14:11:89:522:125:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:main data limitation is that pre-modification principal balance and monthly payment fields are rounded in
9:351:27898:11:11:89:522:114:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the Treasury HAMP file, which introduces a discrepancy between the same loans in both files. Another
9:352:27998:11:11:89:522:103:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:limitation is that the Treasury file required new reporting processes for participating servicers, and the
9:353:28104:11:11:89:522:92:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:reporting requirements changed several times as the program developed. As a result, Treasury explains that
9:354:28210:11:0:89:465:81:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:there are occasional inaccuracies in the underlying data (U.S. Department of Treasury 2014).
10:355:28303:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:design to identify the causal impact of principal reduction on default in the presence of
10:356:28392:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:incomplete matching, we need the match rate to be smooth at the cuto-. We show that
10:357:28475:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:this is the case in online Appendix Figure 1. In Section 4.2 we show that our consumption
10:358:28564:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:result is unchanged (though slightly less precise) when we estimate it using the subsample
10:359:28654:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of borrowers in the bank dataset, which does not rely on matching and is described in the
10:360:28743:17:22:89:171:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:following section.
10:361:28761:22:27:89:248:604:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:2.2  JPMCI Bank Dataset
10:362:28784:27:16:106:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our seconddataset includes de-identified account-level monthly information on all mort-
10:363:28871:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:gages serviced by Chase bank and spending by mortgagors who also had a Chase credit card.
10:364:28960:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:The dataset covers 2009 to 2016. We focus on two subsamples of borrowers. The sample we
10:365:29047:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:use as a robustness check to study the e-ect of principal reduction on consumption includes
10:366:29138:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:all HAMP borrowers with both a mortgage and a credit card with Chase. We observe credit
10:367:29225:16:16:89:445:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:card spending for 22,924 borrowers one year before and after modification.
10:368:29299:16:17:106:523:479:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The sample we use to study the e-ect of payment reduction includes all borrowers who
10:369:29383:17:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:receive either a government-subsidized HAMP or private modification. This includes 60,000
10:370:29472:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:mortgages owned or securitized by Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac (the GSEs) and 86,000
10:371:29554:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:mortgages which are owned or have been securitized by Chase.  We limit the sample to
10:372:29638:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications performed in the fourth quarter of 2011 or later, when the particular versions
10:373:29730:17:16:89:523:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of the private programs we study were su-ciently established.12We analyze the impacts
10:374:29815:16:28:89:434:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:on GSE-backed and non-GSE-backed mortgages separately in Section 5.
10:375:29882:28:30:89:399:352:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:3  E-ect of Principal Reduction on Default
10:376:29924:30:16:106:521:322:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In this section we analyze the e-ect of principal reduction on borrower default.We
10:377:30006:16:17:89:522:306:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:compare borrowers who received two di-erent types of government-subsidized modifications,
10:378:30095:17:16:89:522:289:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:with both types receiving identical short-term payment reductions but one type receiving
10:379:30183:16:17:89:522:273:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:additional principal reduction. Using a regression discontinuity empirical strategy we find
10:380:30274:17:16:89:522:256:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that substantial principal reductions have no e-ect. We can rule out prior cross-sectional
10:381:30364:16:23:89:320:240:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:estimates that were used to justify the program.
10:382:30412:23:17:89:522:217:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:F:3.1  Variation in Payment and Principal Reduction in the Home A-ord-
10:383:30480:17:26:119:277:200:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:able Modification Program
10:384:30505:26:16:106:523:174:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The government instituted the HAMP program in 2009 as a response to the foreclosure
10:385:30588:16:17:89:522:158:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:crisis. It provided government subsidies to help facilitate mortgage modifications for borrow-
10:386:30682:17:16:89:522:141:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ers struggling to make their payments. In total, 1.7 million borrowers received modifications
10:387:30775:16:17:89:192:125:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:through the program.
10:388:30795:17:16:106:523:108:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The government designed HAMP’s eligibility criteria to target the borrowers it perceived
10:389:30883:16:14:98:523:92:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:12Both Chase and the GSEs had a variety of other private modification programs with di-erent designs
10:390:30983:14:0:89:178:78:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:that preceded HAMP.
11:391:31003:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:as most likely to benefit from modifications. Borrowers must have current payments greater
11:392:31093:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:than 31 percent of their income, be delinquent or in imminent default at the time of their
11:393:31183:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:application, attest that they are facing a financial hardship that makes it di-cult to continue
11:394:31278:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:making mortgage payments, and report that they do not have enough liquid assets to
11:395:31360:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:maintain their current debt payments and living expenses. In almost all cases, borrowers
11:396:31448:17:16:89:437:626:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:must be owner-occupants and have loan balances of less than $730,000.13
11:397:31519:16:17:106:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The primary goal of HAMP modifications is to provide borrowers with more a-ordable
11:398:31601:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:mortgages. All borrowers who receive modifications have their payment reduced to reach
11:399:31687:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a 31 percent Payment-to-Income (PTI) ratio for at least five years.  This rule results in
11:400:31776:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:substantial modifications for many borrowers. The mean payment reduction is $680 per
11:401:31860:17:16:89:391:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:month, or 38 percent of the borrower’s prior monthly payment.
11:402:31921:16:17:106:523:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our research design relies on contrasting borrowers assigned to two distinct modification
11:403:32010:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:types. Both modification types result in the same payment reduction for the first five years,
11:404:32103:16:17:89:400:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:but each type achieves this payment reduction in a di-erent way.
11:405:32167:17:16:106:523:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The first modification type provides what we call a “payment reduction” modification.
11:406:32252:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Figure 1a shows the average annual payments for borrowers in this modification type relative
11:407:32344:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to their payments under the status quo. This modification implements up to three steps
11:408:32430:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to achieve the 31 percent PTI target. First, the interest rate is reduced down to a floor
11:409:32519:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of two percent for a period of five years, after which it gradually increases to the market
11:410:32610:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rate. Second, if the target is not reached after the interest rate reduction, the mortgage
11:411:32700:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:maturity is extended up to 40 years. Third, if the target still is not reached, a portion of
11:412:32792:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the unpaid balance is converted into a non interest-bearing balloon payment due at the end
11:413:32882:16:16:89:194:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of the mortgage term.
11:414:32903:16:17:106:523:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The second modification type is what we call a “payment and principal reduction”
11:415:32983:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification (also known as the HAMP Principal Reduction Alternative). The first step in
11:416:33071:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:this modification is to forgive a borrower’s unpaid principal balance until the new monthly
11:417:33162:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payment achieves the 31 percent PTI target or their LTV ratio hits 115 percent, whichever
11:418:33251:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:comes first. If the borrower’s monthly payment is still above the target, then the interest
11:419:33342:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rate reduction, maturity extension, and principal forbearance steps described above are
11:420:33429:16:17:89:411:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:followed as needed. 241,000 borrowers received these modifications.
11:421:33496:17:16:106:523:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The government introduced these principal reduction modifications in 2010 in response to
11:422:33584:16:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:growing concern that debt levels, rather than just debt payments, were responsible for high
11:423:33675:16:17:89:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:default rates and depressed consumption. The government devoted substantial resources
11:424:33760:17:16:89:522:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:towards supporting principal reduction modifications.  On average, the government paid
11:425:33846:16:17:89:522:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:an additional $21,000 per modification to support modifications with principal reduction
11:426:33934:17:16:89:238:133:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:(Scharlemann and Shore 2016).
11:427:33963:16:15:98:522:117:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:13These criteria rule out borrowers who might be particularly likely to strategically default. However,
11:428:34066:15:11:89:522:102:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:such borrowers are responsible for a small share of defaults. Eighty-seven percent of defaults in 2009 were
11:429:34173:11:11:89:522:91:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:for owner-occupied mortgages (Agarwal et al. (2017a) Table 1) and combining the SCF and the PSID we
11:430:34272:11:0:89:414:80:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:calculate that 95 percent of defaults were for loans below this balance threshold.
12:431:34355:0:17:106:523:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:By comparing borrowers who receive these two types of modifications, we can estimate
12:432:34439:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the e-ect of long-term debt obligations holding short-term payments constant. The two
12:433:34524:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:types of modifications have identical e-ects on payments in the short term, but dramati-
12:434:34612:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cally di-erent e-ects on long-term payments and homeowner equity. Figure 1a shows that
12:435:34698:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payment reductions are identical for the first five years, after which payments rise more
12:436:34787:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sharply for borrowers with payment reduction modifications. Figure 1b summarizes the fi-
12:437:34875:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:nancial impacts of these modifications for borrowers in our sample. Borrowers with principal
12:438:34967:17:16:89:475:593:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:reduction modifications receive an average of $67,000 more principal reduction.14
12:439:35048:16:16:106:523:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The monetary value of the principal reduction depends on borrower behavior.  To a
12:440:35129:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrower who prepays her mortgage the next day, principal reduction is worth $67,000,
12:441:35214:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:but it is worth nothing to a borrower who immediately defaults and never repays.  We
12:442:35298:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:calculate the value to borrowers using two methods. First, we calculate that the incremental
12:443:35390:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction in the Net Present Value (NPV) of payments owed under the mortgage contract
12:444:35475:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:if the borrower repays on schedule is $34,000. This calculation assumes borrowers discount
12:445:35565:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:future cash flows at the average market interest rate, consistent with the empirical findings
12:446:35658:16:16:89:271:462:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:in Busse et al. (2013) for auto loans.15
12:447:35698:16:17:106:523:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Second, we calculate the NPV of expected payments using observed prepayment and
12:448:35777:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:default behavior of HAMP borrowers. For default, we use a lifetime liquidation rate of 32%
12:449:35867:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:based on public HAMP performance data and provide details on our valuation method in
12:450:35951:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:online Appendix C.1. Prepayment raises the NPV and default lowers it. The default e-ect
12:451:36038:16:17:89:360:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:dominates and we calculate a change in NPV of $28,000.
12:452:36092:17:16:106:523:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Program administrators took steps to ensure that borrowers understood the new mort-
12:453:36175:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:gage terms. The cover letter for the modification agreement prominently listed the new
12:454:36261:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:interest rate, mortgage term, and amount of principal reduction. Additionally, the modi-
12:455:36349:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:fication agreement included a summary showing the new monthly payment each year, as
12:456:36432:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:shown in online Appendix Figure 2.  Borrowers appear eager to take up modifications.
12:457:36516:17:23:89:506:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Conditional on being o-ered a modification, 97 percent of borrowers accepted the o-er.
12:458:36602:23:16:89:528:258:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:3.2  Identification: Discontinuity in Principal Reduction at Treasury Model
12:459:36677:16:27:119:157:242:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f16:?:Cuto-
12:460:36682:27:16:106:523:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:During the Great Recession, there were concerns that a large share of defaults were
12:461:36765:16:17:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:“strategic” in nature, committed by borrowers who only had negative equity rather than by
12:462:36854:17:16:89:523:182:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers with a-ordability problems (Zingales 2010, Winkler 2010, Experian and Wyman
12:463:36939:16:15:98:522:166:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:14Some borrowers in the payment reduction modification type received small amounts of principal reduc-
12:464:37041:15:11:89:522:151:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:tion. This is because some servicers wanted to provide principal forgiveness outside of the Treasury incentive
12:465:37151:11:11:89:522:140:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:program, which only paid incentives for forgiveness above 105 percent LTV and required the forgiveness to
12:466:37256:11:7:89:174:129:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:vest over three years.
12:467:37278:7:15:98:522:122:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:15This is also consistent with a “market-based” conception of wealth where valuation does not di-er across
12:468:37384:15:11:89:522:107:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:individuals. However, for an individual conception of wealth, the gains are still substantial even for a more
12:469:37493:11:11:89:522:96:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:impatient borrower. For example, if instead we assume the borrower’s discount rate is twice the mortgage
12:470:37597:11:0:89:499:85:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:interest rate, principal forgiveness reduces the NPV of payments owed under the contract by $18,000.
13:471:37699:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:2009). To assess the extent of strategic default, the ideal experiment would randomly assign
13:472:37791:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers to di-erent levels ofnegativeequity holding fixed immediate monthly payments.
13:473:37878:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:As in HAMP, in this ideal experiment the treatment group would remain slightly underwater
13:474:37967:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:even after principal reduction. This is because bringing borrowers above water may enable
13:475:38056:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers to avoid default by selling the home or borrowing against the home (Gupta and
13:476:38143:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Hansman 2018), and hence would not be informative about the prevalence of strategic
13:477:38226:16:17:89:125:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:default.
13:478:38234:17:16:106:523:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In lieu of this ideal experiment, we have a setting in HAMP where borrower assignment
13:479:38319:16:16:89:523:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to di-erent levels of negative equity is determined in part by a cuto-rule, and in part by
13:480:38409:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:servicer and lender type. This assignment generates quasi-experimental variation in which
13:481:38498:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications borrowers receive, which we will exploit in our empirical strategies. We discuss
13:482:38592:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the cuto-rule–which we use in a regression discontinuity to estimate the impact of principal
13:483:38684:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction on default–in this section. We use variation in servicer and lender type to estimate
13:484:38778:16:17:89:491:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:consumption impacts, and so we defer an explanation of that variation to Section 4.
13:485:38861:17:16:106:523:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our quasi-experimental variation covers the period with the most severe delinquency
13:486:38944:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rates in the recent crisis. Our sample of borrowers have their first delinquencies in the fourth
13:487:39040:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:quarter of 2009, just before the peak of the delinquency crisis, which did not begin abating
13:488:39132:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:until 2013. Online Appendix Figure 3 plots the delinquency rate for all U.S. borrowers over
13:489:39223:16:17:89:113:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:time.
13:490:39228:17:16:106:523:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Principal reduction is determined in part by a calculation examining which modification
13:491:39315:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:type is expected to be most beneficial for the lender.  Using a model developed by the
13:492:39401:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:U.S. Treasury Department, servicers calculate the expected NPV of cash flows for lenders
13:493:39489:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:under the status quo and under each of the two modification options.  The NPV model
13:494:39572:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:takes into consideration government-provided incentives as well as the expected impact that
13:495:39663:17:16:89:334:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications will have on default and prepayment.
13:496:39713:16:17:106:523:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our empirical strategy exploits a large jump in the share of borrowers receiving modifi-
13:497:39801:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cations with principal reductions when the NPV model shows it will be more beneficial to
13:498:39889:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:lenders than the alternative. This jump is shown in Figure 2a. The purpose of the Treasury
13:499:39979:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:NPV model is to reduce contracting frictions between lenders and servicers. Servicers are
13:500:40068:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:bound by their fiduciary duty to the lenders to maximize repayment, and as a result are
13:501:40155:17:16:89:455:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:more likely to o-er the modifications shown to be most beneficial to lenders.
13:502:40232:16:16:106:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We identify the e-ect of principal reduction on default using the cuto-in the expected
13:503:40318:16:17:89:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:benefit to lenders with a regression discontinuity research design. Let the receipt of principal
13:504:40414:17:16:89:522:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction treatment be denoted by the dummy variableTœ{0,1},where0represents
13:505:40490:16:17:89:522:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:receiving a payment reduction modification, and letXcapture the characteristics of the
13:506:40576:17:16:89:522:133:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrower. The Treasury NPV model calculates the expected net present value to lenders
13:507:40661:16:0:89:522:117:119:g_d0_f18:119:g_d0_f4:B:ENPV(T,X)under either scenario. Our running variableVis the normalized predicted
14:508:40743:0:32:89:398:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:gain to lenders of providing principal reduction to borrowers, i.e.

14:510:40815:0:15:254:396:684:119:g_d0_f18:119:g_d0_f21:?:ENPV(1,X)≠ENPV(0,X)
14:511:40834:15:0:293:357:669:119:g_d0_f18:119:g_d0_f21:?:ENPV(0,X)
14:512:40843:0:32:397:522:677:119:g_d0_f18:119:g_d0_f4:A:.(1)
14:513:40847:32:17:89:523:645:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:A realizationvreflects the expected percent gain to the lender from principal reduction
14:514:40934:17:16:89:522:628:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:relative to a standard modification.  The cuto-that a-ects assignment to treatment or
14:515:41019:16:17:89:522:612:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:control is atv=0.  These are borrowers for whom the increased government incentive
14:516:41101:17:16:89:522:595:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payments and the reduction in default expected by the Treasury NPV model generate gains
14:517:41188:16:17:89:523:579:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to lenders that o-set lenders’ cash-flow loss from forgiving principal.  We normalize the
14:518:41277:17:16:89:522:562:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:predicted gain to avoid a high concentration of low-balance mortgages near the cuto-,
14:519:41362:16:16:89:523:546:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:though our key finding that principal reduction does not a-ect default is insensitive to this
14:520:41455:16:17:89:158:530:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:normalization.
14:521:41469:17:16:106:522:513:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The treatment e-ect of receiving principal reduction is determined by the jump in default
