14:546:43211:22:26:89:411:114:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:3.3  Results: E-ect of Principal Reduction on Default
14:547:43264:26:16:106:523:88:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Figure 2a shows that there is a discontinuous jump of 41 percentage points in the share
14:548:43351:16:0:89:522:72:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of borrowers receiving principal reduction at the cuto-. Measured in terms of dollars of
15:549:43441:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction, the treatment size at the cuto-is $30,000. This reduces borrower LTV
15:550:43530:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:by 11 percentage points, and amounts to a $17,000 reduction in the NPV of borrower pay-
15:551:43617:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ments owed over the full mortgage term. Importantly, there is no jump in monthly payment
15:552:43705:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction at the cuto-, highlighting that the “treatment” we are analyzing is a reduction in
15:553:43797:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:mortgage principal that leaves short-term payments unchanged. The relationship of the four
15:554:43887:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:aforementioned variables with respect to the running variable is shown in online Appendix
15:555:43976:16:17:89:132:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Figure 6.
15:556:43985:17:16:106:523:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We find that principal reduction has no impact on default. Figure 2b shows the reduced
15:557:44071:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:form of the fuzzy regression discontinuity specification, plotting the default rate against the
15:558:44166:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:running variable. We define our main measure of default as being 90 days delinquent at
15:559:44252:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:any point between modification date and March 2015, when our dataset ends, which is an
15:560:44338:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:average of three years. This is the measure of default used to disqualify a borrower from the
15:561:44431:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP program and is the common measure used in the prior literature discussed in section
15:562:44519:16:17:89:523:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:3.4. There is no jump in default rates at the cuto-. Our point estimate is that $30,000 of
15:563:44609:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction changes default probabilities by less than one percentage point, and we
15:564:44700:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:can rule out a reduction of more than five percentage points. Online Appendix Figure 7
15:565:44786:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:shows that our estimates are close to zero for a wide range of bandwidth choices, and these
15:566:44877:17:16:89:382:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:results are discussed in more detail in online Appendix B.1.2.
15:567:44939:16:17:106:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our evidence suggests that principal reduction is also ine-ective at reducing foreclosures.
15:568:45030:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Online Appendix Figure 8 shows that there is no jump in the foreclosure initiation rate at
15:569:45120:16:17:89:523:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the cuto-.16It is not surprising that the same pattern would be seen in foreclosures as in
15:570:45210:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:defaults. Borrowers who have defaulted and are unable to self-cure are generally unable to
15:571:45300:16:16:89:387:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sell their home to avoid foreclosure while they are underwater.
15:572:45363:16:17:106:523:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our results imply a large government cost per avoided foreclosure. The upper bound of
15:573:45448:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:our 95 percent confidence interval suggests foreclosure initiations were reduced at most by
15:574:45539:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:3.6 percentage points. Herkenho-and Ohanian (2015) document that approximately half
15:575:45622:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of borrowers with a foreclosure initiation end up with a completed foreclosure, while the
15:576:45711:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:other half self-cure. This suggests that principal reduction reduced foreclosure completions
15:577:45803:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:by at most 1.8 percentage points during the window we study.17The government spent
15:578:45885:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:about $10,000 per modification to support the additional principal reduction of the size we
15:579:45976:17:16:89:522:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:analyze in our treatment group. This translates into a government cost of at least $556,000
15:580:46067:16:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:per avoided foreclosure, more than an order of magnitude larger than common estimates of
15:581:46155:16:17:89:501:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the social costs of foreclosure (Department of Housing and Urban Development 2010).
15:582:46238:17:16:106:523:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:It is possible that foreclosures would have been mechanically avoided by bringing bor-
15:583:46324:16:15:98:522:150:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:16Due to the lengthy delay between foreclosure initiations and foreclosure completions, foreclosure com-
15:584:46428:15:7:89:289:135:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:pletions are rarely observed in our sample period.
15:585:46478:7:14:98:522:128:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:17Although we find little impact on foreclosures within our three-year analysis window, it is possible that
15:586:46585:14:11:89:522:114:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:once these borrowers regain positive equity several years in the future, foreclosures for the principal reduction
15:587:46698:11:11:89:522:103:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:group will be lower than for those who did not receive it. Unfortunately this is not something we can analyze
15:588:46807:11:11:89:522:92:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:with the data in this paper. Furthermore, to the extent that the policy goal was short-term housing market
15:589:46913:11:0:89:356:81:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:stabilization, the benefit of future foreclosure reduction is unclear.
16:590:46985:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rowers all the way into positive equity, but this also would have been an expensive strategy
16:591:47077:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:after prices had fallen substantially. The average underwater borrower evaluated for prin-
16:592:47167:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cipal reduction had about $100,000 in negative equity. Even if foreclosure initiations were
16:593:47258:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:completely eliminated by forgiving 100 percent of this negative equity (since defaulting bor-
16:594:47351:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rowers could sell their home and avoid a foreclosure), this would require $2.5 million in
16:595:47440:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:writedowns to avoid a subsequent foreclosure initiation and $5 million to avoid a foreclosure
16:596:47533:16:23:89:144:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:completion.
16:597:47544:23:26:89:366:587:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:3.4  Comparison to Prior Evidence on Default
16:598:47588:26:17:106:523:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our results are inconsistent with prior evidence based on cross-sectional relationships.
16:599:47676:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:For example, Haughwout et al. (2016) use data on modifications performed prior to HAMP
16:600:47762:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and find using cross-sectional variation that borrowers who received principal reductions
16:601:47851:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:equivalent to ours saw an 18 percentage point reduction in default. Furthermore, there is a
16:602:47942:16:16:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:strong cross-sectional relationship between the amount of negative equity and default rates
16:603:48033:16:17:89:288:479:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:across all borrowers (Gerardi et al. 2015).
16:604:48076:17:16:106:523:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Indeed, the U.S. Treasury Department developed a model based on this historical data
16:605:48160:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that predicts a substantial reduction in default from principal reduction, which is inconsis-
16:606:48253:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:tent with our findings. The Treasury generated this estimate as part of its model to predict
16:607:48345:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the benefits of modifications to lenders (Holden et al. 2012). We implement the Treasury
16:608:48433:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:redefault model (U.S. Department of the Treasury 2015) in the public HAMP data and
16:609:48515:16:16:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:calculate the predicted impact of principal reduction at the cuto-. The Treasury model
16:610:48601:16:17:89:522:364:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:expects a sharp reduction in default of 6.6 percentage points at the NPV cuto-, which we
16:611:48689:17:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:can rule out using the lower bound of our 95 percent confidence interval. This implies that
16:612:48780:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:many lenders were actually worse o-from having o-ered principal reduction, since the ex-
16:613:48868:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:pected reduction in defaults necessary to o-set the reduced cash flow from borrowers did
16:614:48956:16:17:89:164:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:not materialize.
16:615:48972:17:16:106:523:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Why is our causal estimate so much smaller than what is predicted by the cross-sectional
16:616:49060:16:16:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:relationship between borrower equity and default and models calibrated to this relationship?
16:617:49152:16:17:89:522:249:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:One possibility is that the cross-sectional evidence was misleading because borrowers with
16:618:49242:17:16:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:less equity were also borrowers who purchased homes near the height of the credit boom and
16:619:49332:16:17:89:522:216:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:who therefore might have been less credit-worthy on other dimensions. Palmer (2015) shows
16:620:49421:17:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that changes in borrower and loan characteristics can explain 40 percent of the di-erence in
16:621:49513:16:17:89:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:default rates between the 2003-2004 and the 2006-2007 cohorts. Another possibility is that
16:622:49603:17:16:89:522:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the large price reductions that left many borrowers underwater were also correlated with
16:623:49691:16:17:89:522:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:other omitted economic shocks that themselves could be responsible for higher default rates
16:624:49782:17:16:89:190:133:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:(Adelino et al. 2016).
16:625:49804:16:16:106:523:117:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In contrast to these cross-sectional estimates, Scharlemann and Shore (2016) analyze
16:626:49888:16:0:89:522:101:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction in HAMP using a regression kink design, and also find that principal
17:627:49978:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction is a costly way to reduce defaults.18Our empirical results reinforce the conclusions
17:628:50072:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of Scharlemann and Shore (2016) using an alternative estimation strategy that requires
17:629:50158:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:weaker parametric assumptions. In Scharlemann and Shore (2016)’s preferred specification,
17:630:50247:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:they use a regression kink design and assume that the relationship between the running
17:631:50333:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:variable and the outcome variable is globally linear. In contrast, our regression discontinuity
17:632:50428:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:identification strategy assumes that unobservable borrower traits are smooth in the local
17:633:50517:16:28:89:207:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:region around the cuto-.
17:634:50541:28:30:89:441:582:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:4  E-ect of Principal Reduction on Consumption
17:635:50587:30:16:106:522:552:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In this section we explore the e-ect of principal reductions on consumption. We find
17:636:50671:16:17:89:522:536:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that the marginal propensity to consume out of housing wealth for underwater borrowers
17:637:50757:17:16:89:522:519:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:is an order of magnitude smaller than the marginal propensity to consume for average
17:638:50841:16:23:89:275:503:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:homeowners examined in prior studies.
17:639:50878:23:26:89:498:480:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:4.1  Identification: Panel Di-erence-in-Di-erence Empirical Strategy
17:640:50946:26:17:106:522:454:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our use of consumption data motivates a change in research design to a panel di-erence-
17:641:51033:17:16:89:522:437:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in-di-erences strategy for two reasons. First, our regression discontinuity strategy is under-
17:642:51127:16:17:89:529:421:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:powered for studying changes in consumption. Economically meaningful consumption changes
17:643:51215:17:16:89:522:404:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:can not be ruled out in the regression discontinuity sample given lack of precision. As we
17:644:51305:16:16:89:522:388:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:discuss in more detail in Section 4.3, even a small change in consumption on the order of
17:645:51394:16:17:89:522:372:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:five percent of the amount of principal forgiven would be meaningful relative to average
17:646:51482:17:16:89:522:355:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:marginal propensities to consume out of housing wealth changes studied in other contexts,
17:647:51571:16:17:89:522:339:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:whereas the predicted impacts on default from the prior literature were much larger. The
17:648:51659:17:16:89:522:322:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:second reason is that the panel nature of the spending measures from our credit bureau
17:649:51745:16:17:89:522:306:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and banking data allow us to exploit an alternative strategy that o-ers more precision.
17:650:51832:17:16:89:523:289:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Lagged spending measures allow us to adjust for underlying di-erences between borrowers
17:651:51919:16:17:89:522:273:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:receiving di-erent modification types within a wider bandwidth than with the regression
17:652:52006:17:16:89:522:256:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:discontinuity. These factors favor a panel di-erence-in-di-erences design, though we also
17:653:52095:16:16:89:365:240:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:report results from the regression discontinuity strategy.19
17:654:52155:16:17:106:523:224:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our panel di-erence-in-di-erences design uses as a control group the set of underwater
17:655:52241:17:16:89:522:207:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers who were eligible for principal reductions, but who instead received only payment
17:656:52332:16:17:89:522:191:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction modifications. This design relies on the fact that borrowers who receive payment
17:657:52422:17:16:89:522:174:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction modifications experience the same short-term payment reductions as borrowers
17:658:52508:16:14:98:522:158:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:18In their preferred specification, where they use the global relationship between default and principal
17:659:52612:14:11:89:522:144:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:reduction, they find that principal reduction of the size we estimate (reducing the LTV by 11 points) reduces
17:660:52721:11:11:89:522:133:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:default by 1.9 percentage points, a result that is within our confidence interval. When using data close to
17:661:52828:11:7:89:522:122:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the kink, they find that principal reduction has no statistically or economically significant e-ect on default.
17:662:52939:7:15:98:522:115:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:19We also have lagged measures of default from the credit bureau data. However, a di-erence-in-di-erences
17:663:53044:15:11:89:523:100:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:design is not valid for default because pre-treatment di-erences in the levels of default are mechanically
17:664:53150:11:11:89:522:89:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:removed at modification date, at which point all loans become current.  This means that the change in
17:665:53251:11:0:89:479:78:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:default for the control group is not a valid counterfactual for the change in the treatment group.
18:666:53351:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:who receive principal reduction, but receive substantially less generous long-term payment
18:667:53441:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:relief. Summary statistics for both groups are shown in online Appendix Table 2.20The
18:668:53526:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:size of short-term payment reductions are nearly identical across groups, but borrowers
18:669:53613:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:who receive payment and principal reduction modifications receive on average $67,000 more
18:670:53702:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction, reducing the NPV of the payments owed under their mortgage contract
18:671:53790:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:by an additional $34,000. In accordance with the HAMP rules described in the previous
18:672:53875:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:section, borrowers who received principal forgiveness remained underwater (usually at 115
18:673:53964:17:16:89:523:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:percent LTV). Thus, the treatment is the e-ect of long-term debt forgiveness holding short-
18:674:54055:16:16:89:300:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:term payments and access to liquidity fixed.
18:675:54099:16:17:106:523:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our identification comes from cross-servicer and cross-lender variation in the propensity
18:676:54188:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to provide principal reductions given observed borrower characteristics. Borrowers are not
18:677:54278:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:assigned to principal reduction modifications according to the NPV calculation alone because
18:678:54370:17:16:89:523:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:di-erent lenders have di-erent views about principal reduction and servicers are not always
18:679:54461:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:confident they have the contractual right to forgive principal or the capacity to manage
18:680:54549:17:16:89:523:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the process.21Conditional on lender and servicer, all borrowers are treated alike. Servicers
18:681:54641:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:must submit a written policy to the Treasury department detailing when they will o-er
18:682:54726:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction modifications and attesting that they will treat all observably similar
18:683:54817:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers alike (U.S. Department of Treasury 2014). Intuitively, comparing borrowers across
18:684:54908:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification types relies on servicer-lenders that were more likely to o-er principal reduction
18:685:55003:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:not having borrowers whose consumption was trending di-erentially relative to borrowers
18:686:55090:16:17:89:403:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:whose servicer-lenders were less likely to o-er principal reduction.
18:687:55158:17:16:106:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The key identifying assumption for the panel di-erence-in-di-erences design is that con-
18:688:55246:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sumption trends would be the same in both groups in the absence of treatment.  This
18:689:55329:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:assumption is plausible when the two groups exhibit parallel trends before treatment. We
18:690:55417:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:show this visually in Figure 3a, which plots mean credit card expenditure around modifica-
18:691:55507:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:tion date.22The same figure shows that principal reduction appears to have little e-ect–a
18:692:55596:17:16:89:299:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:result we explore in a regression framework.
18:693:55640:16:30:106:338:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Formally, our main specification is the following:
18:694:55690:30:18:122:522:235:119:g_d0_f18:119:g_d0_f4:A:yi,g,t,s=“g+“t+“m(i),s+—(Principal Reductiong◊Postt)+xÕit”+Ái,g,t,s,(3)
18:695:55761:18:15:98:522:217:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:20Our main sample for this analysis includes underwater borrowers in the matched HAMP credit bureau
18:696:55860:15:11:89:522:202:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:dataset who are observed one year before and after modification and report positive credit card expenditure
18:697:55967:11:7:89:259:191:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:in at least one month during this window.
18:698:56008:7:15:98:522:184:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:21The contractual frictions are particularly acute with securitized loans. For example, Kruger (2018) shows
18:699:56115:15:11:89:522:169:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:that 22 percent of servicing agreements governing securitized pools explicitly forbid servicers from reducing
18:700:56224:11:11:89:522:158:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:principal balances as part of modifications.  As a result, principal reduction in HAMP was less common
18:701:56326:11:10:89:522:147:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:among borrowers in securitized pools (Scharlemann and Shore 2016).  Conversely, principal reduction is
18:702:56428:10:11:89:522:137:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:more common for loans held on banks’ own balance sheets, where servicer-lender frictions are mitigated
18:703:56530:11:8:89:177:126:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:(Agarwal et al. 2011).
18:704:56552:8:14:98:522:118:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:22Online Appendix Figure 9a normalizes expenditure to zero at modification date in order to more clearly
18:705:56656:14:11:89:522:104:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:show the parallel pre-trends. Online Appendix Figure 9b plots mean auto expenditure around modification
18:706:56759:11:0:89:298:93:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:date and similarly demonstrates parallel pre-trends.
19:707:56813:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:whereidenotes borrowers,gœ{payment reduction, payment & principal reduction}the
19:708:56892:17:16:89:523:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification group,tthe number of months since modification,sthe calendar month, and
19:709:56976:16:17:89:521:676:119:g_d0_f18:64:g_d0_f23:F:mthe household’s Metropolitan Statistical Area (MSA). Our main outcome variablesyi,g,t,s
19:710:57064:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:are monthly credit card and auto expenditure, which proxy for non-durable and durable

19:725:58084:22:27:89:446:440:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:4.2  Results: E-ect of Principal Reduction on Consumption
19:726:58141:27:16:106:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We find that neither credit card nor auto expenditures are a-ected by principal reduction
19:727:58230:16:16:89:522:397:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in the year after modification. Our main results are reported in Panels A and B of Table
19:728:58318:16:17:89:522:381:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:2.  In both panels, column (1) reports the most sparse specification, while columns (2)-
19:729:58406:17:16:89:522:364:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:(6) add in additional fixed e-ects and controls.  Across all specifications, the treatment
19:730:58496:16:17:89:522:348:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:e-ect of principal reduction on both monthly credit card and auto expenditure is small and
19:731:58586:17:16:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:statistically insignificant. Our preferred estimate using equation 3 is in column (6), which
19:732:58678:16:17:89:523:315:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:includes MSA by calendar month fixed e-ects and interacts control variables with a post-
19:733:58766:17:16:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification dummy. In this specification, our point estimate is that principal reduction
19:734:58855:16:17:89:522:282:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of $67,000 increases borrower monthly credit card expenditure by less than $2 and auto
19:735:58941:17:16:89:215:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:spending by less than $10.
19:736:58967:16:16:106:523:249:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f4:A:Robustness– We address two potential weaknesses of the credit bureau data by con-
19:737:59048:16:17:89:522:233:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:firming that the result also holds in the JPMCI bank dataset. The first potential weakness
19:738:59138:17:16:89:522:216:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:is that credit card expenditure is inferred from other variables reported by servicers, as
19:739:59228:16:17:89:522:200:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:discussed in Section 2.1. The second is any measurement error introduced by our matching
19:740:59316:17:16:89:523:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:procedure. The JPMCI dataset covers only one servicer, but does not su-er from either
19:741:59401:16:15:89:522:167:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of these two potential limitations.  It includes credit card data but not auto loan data.
19:742:59490:15:15:98:522:152:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:23This includes the predicted gain to lenders from providing principal reduction, the predicted gain inter-
19:743:59597:15:11:89:522:137:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:acted with a dummy variable equal to one when the gain is positive, borrower characteristics (credit score,
19:744:59704:11:11:89:522:126:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:monthly income, non-housing monthly debt payment), pre-modification loan characteristics (LTV, principal
19:745:59808:11:11:89:522:115:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:balance, PTI, monthly payment), property value, origination LTV, and monthly payment reduction. By
19:746:59906:11:11:89:522:104:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:controlling for the predicted gain to lenders of providing principal reduction, the main di-erence between
19:747:60012:11:11:89:522:93:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:our regression discontinuity and di-erence-in-di-erences strategies is that the regression discontinuity strat-
19:748:60123:11:10:89:522:82:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f9:F:egy instruments for treatment with the jump in the probability of receiving principal reduction at the cuto-
19:749:60231:10:0:89:493:72:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:while the di-erence-in-di-erences strategy uses all the variation conditional on the running variable.
20:750:60335:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Online Appendix Figure 10 shows that the same pattern of credit card expenditure around
20:751:60422:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification date holds in the JPMCI data. Our estimated treatment e-ects are displayed
20:752:60509:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in online Appendix Table 3. Here again we find the treatment e-ect of debt forgiveness on
20:753:60598:17:16:89:384:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:credit card expenditure is small and statistically insignificant.
20:754:60663:16:17:106:523:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We also explore the e-ect of principal reduction on consumption using our regression
20:755:60747:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:discontinuity strategy.  Our outcome variables are the change in mean credit card and
20:756:60832:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:auto spending from the 12 months before modification to the 12 months after modification.
20:757:60921:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:The reduced form plots are shown in online Appendix Figure 11. These plots confirm the
20:758:61007:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:weakness of this strategy for studying consumption impacts since the strategy su-ers from
20:759:61096:16:17:89:177:561:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:lack of precision.24
20:760:61116:17:16:106:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We are unable to analyze the long-run e-ects of principal reduction on consumption
20:761:61198:16:17:89:469:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:within our sample window. We discuss potential long-run e-ects in Section 7.2.
20:762:61276:17:16:106:522:511:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f4:A:E-ect of Payment Reduction on Consumption –A natural concern with our
20:763:61345:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:zero result is that our consumption series might not detect responses to important financial
20:764:61437:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:changes. However, the paths of credit card and auto spending around modification suggest
20:765:61525:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that borrowers do seem to respond to short-term payment reductions. Both credit card and
20:766:61613:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:auto spending are declining before modification and recover after modification. The decline
20:767:61704:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:pre-modification is likely a result of financial stress experienced by the borrowers. The slope
20:768:61799:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of expenditure changes sharply around modification, suggesting that lower payments help
20:769:61886:17:16:89:199:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:expenditure to recover.
20:770:61909:16:17:106:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The apparent positive e-ect of short-term payment reductions on auto spending is con-
20:771:61994:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sistent with findings in Agarwal et al. (2017a). That paper exploits regional variation in the
20:772:62088:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:implementation of HAMP to estimate the e-ects of HAMP modifications which combine
20:773:62169:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:both short-term and long-term payment reductions. They find that the combined modi-
20:774:62252:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:fications are associated with increased auto spending. If the e-ect of long-term payment
20:775:62340:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reductions in HAMP is zero, as suggested by our estimates, it makes sense to infer that
20:776:62427:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:short-term payment reductions are responsible for the consumption impact they estimate.
20:777:62514:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:In online Appendix B.2.2 we attempt to directly estimate the impact of short-term payment
20:778:62603:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reductions on consumption using the payment-reduction regression discontinuity identifica-
20:779:62693:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:tion strategy in Section 5, but we conclude that this strategy is under-powered for studying
20:780:62785:17:22:89:193:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:consumption impacts.
20:781:62805:22:17:89:522:193:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:F:4.3  Comparison of Estimated MPC From Principal Reduction to Housing
20:782:62873:17:27:119:201:176:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:Wealth MPCs
20:783:62884:27:16:106:523:149:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:To help interpret the economic significance of our results, we convert our estimate for
20:784:62971:16:16:89:522:133:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the impact on credit card and auto consumption into a marginal propensity to consume
20:785:63055:16:17:89:522:117:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:(MPC) out of housing wealth.  First, we scale up credit card spending to a measure of
20:786:63140:17:15:98:522:100:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:24Translating these estimates to a marginal propensity to consume, as in Section 4.3, our confidence interval
20:787:63249:15:0:89:272:85:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:ranges all the way from -15 cents to 41 cents.
21:788:63297:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:non-auto retail spending to be comparable to Mian et al. (2013). We do this by adjusting
21:789:63385:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:for credit card spending on cards where spending is not reported in the credit bureau data
21:790:63475:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and then multiplying by the ratio of non-auto consumer retail spending to consumer credit
21:791:63564:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:card spending in 2012.25Second, we combine with our auto spending measure, annualize,
21:792:63649:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and divide by the mean incremental amount of principal reduction in the treatment group.
21:793:63737:17:16:106:523:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Using this method, our point estimate is that households increased annual consumption
21:794:63822:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:by 0.3 cents per dollar of principal reduction, with the upper bound of the 95 percent
21:795:63908:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:confidence interval corresponding to 0.8 cents. A similar procedure using results from the
21:796:63998:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:JPMCI bank dataset yields an upper bound of 1.2 cents. If we normalize by the reduction
21:797:64085:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in the NPV of mortgage payments owed under the new mortgage contract rather than the
21:798:64169:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:dollar value of principal reduction, we get a point estimate of 0.5 cents and an upper bound
21:799:64261:16:17:89:146:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of 1.6 cents.
21:800:64274:17:16:106:523:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our estimated MPC out of housing wealth for underwater borrowers is an order of
21:801:64353:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:magnitude smaller than the MPC for average homeowners examined in prior studies. A set
21:802:64439:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of comparison points for our estimates of the impact of principal reduction on consumption
21:803:64529:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:comes from the literature examining the impact of price-driven housing wealth changes.
21:804:64615:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:We present several such estimates in Figure 3b.  Campbell and Cocco (2007) and Mian
21:805:64698:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:et al. (2013) find annual MPCs for homeowners around nine cents per dollar of housing
21:806:64783:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:wealth gain. Aladangady (2017) finds an MPC of five cents and Carroll et al. (2011) find
21:807:64871:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:MPCs between two and ten cents. There is also a wide literature estimating the elasticity
21:808:64960:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of consumption to housing wealth, with findings typically between 0.1 and 0.3 (Guren et al.
21:809:65051:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:2018b, Case et al. 2013, Attanasio et al. 2009, Berger et al. 2018). These elasticities translate
21:810:65148:16:16:89:335:347:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:into MPCs between three and 11 cents per dollar.26
21:811:65198:16:17:106:523:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:While our estimates are already below those measuring the MPC of average households
21:812:65281:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in the prior literature, there is evidence that highly leveraged borrowers are usually even
21:813:65372:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f17:119:g_d0_f4:B:moreresponsive. Mian et al. (2013) find that that households living in zip codes with average
21:814:65465:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:LTV ratios above 90 have MPCs that are twice that of the median household, translating
21:815:65551:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:into an MPC of 18 cents.27This result has been used by policy advocates arguing in favor
21:816:65639:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of principal reduction for underwater borrowers.28However, our evidence suggests that
21:817:65724:16:14:98:522:232:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:25Specifically, our adjustment factor is the product of two ratios: (1) the ratio of the number of credit
21:818:65829:14:11:89:522:218:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:cards in TransUnion to the number of credit cards with spending reported in TransUnion, and (2) the ratio
21:819:65934:11:11:89:522:207:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:of non-auto consumer retail spending in 2012 to total consumer credit card spending in 2012.  The first
21:820:66037:11:11:89:522:196:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:term uses our data, retail spend is from Census, and consumer credit card spending is from Federal Reserve
21:821:66143:11:11:89:522:185:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:Payment Study (Federal Reserve 2014). This gives an adjustment factor of(1.2) (2.5) = 3.1. An alternative
21:822:66248:11:11:89:522:174:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:adjustment multiplying by the ratio of average household monthly non-auto retail spend to the average credit
21:823:66356:11:7:89:399:163:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:card spending we observe in our sample gives the same MPC point estimate.
21:824:66429:7:15:98:522:156:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:26For authors who do not report an MPC, we translate elasticities into MPCs by multiplying them by the
21:825:66531:15:11:89:522:141:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:ratio of personal consumption expenditures from the BEA to housing assets from the Flow of Funds from
21:826:66632:11:7:89:297:130:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:2007 reported in Berger et al. (2018), which is 0.34.
21:827:66685:7:15:98:522:123:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:27Similarly, Disney et al. (2010) analyze panel survey data in the U.K. and find that borrowers who begin
21:828:66790:15:11:89:522:108:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the period underwater and end the period above water, and are thus near the 100 LTV threshold, have high
21:829:66894:11:7:89:189:97:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:MPCs of about 13 cents.
21:830:66917:7:0:98:242:90:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:?:28See discussion in Goldfarb (2012).
22:831:66955:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the response of borrowers who are far underwater, with LTVs far above 90, have much
22:832:67038:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:lower MPCs out of housing wealth, rendering principal reductions for underwater borrowers
22:833:67127:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ine-ective. In Section 7 we argue that the inability of underwater borrowers to monetize
22:834:67215:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:housing wealth can explain the discrepancy between our estimates and those in the prior
22:835:67302:16:25:89:391:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:literature, and we explore the policy implications of this result.
22:836:67368:25:30:89:397:618:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:5  E-ect of Payment Reduction on Default
22:837:67408:30:16:106:522:588:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In this section we analyze the e-ect of liquidity provision on borrower default. In contrast
22:838:67500:16:17:89:522:572:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to our results on the ine-ectiveness of principal reduction, we find that immediate payment
22:839:67591:17:23:89:467:555:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction with no change in long-term obligations significantly reduces default.
22:840:67671:23:17:89:522:532:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:F:5.1  Variation in Payment Reduction Between Government-Subsidized
22:841:67736:17:26:119:272:515:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:and Private Modifications
22:842:67761:26:16:106:522:489:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We analyze the e-ect of immediate payment reduction by comparing borrowers with
22:843:67840:16:17:89:522:473:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:government-subsidized HAMP modifications to those with alternative private modifications.
22:844:67929:17:16:89:522:456:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Although servicers were required to o-er all eligible borrowers HAMP modifications, as
22:845:68015:16:17:89:352:440:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:described in Section 3.1 not all borrowers were eligible.
22:846:68072:17:16:106:523:423:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:To mitigate losses on loans ineligible for HAMP, mortgage owners developed their own
22:847:68156:16:17:89:522:407:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:private modification programs. During the Great Recession, mortgages could be partitioned
22:848:68245:17:16:89:522:390:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:into two approximately equally-sized groups. Loans which met certain underwriting crite-
22:849:68333:16:16:89:522:374:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ria, including a maximum loan size and a minimum borrower FICO score, were usually
22:850:68415:16:17:89:522:358:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:owned or securitized by Fannie Mac and Freddie Mac (the GSEs). Loans which did not
22:851:68497:17:16:89:522:341:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:meet these criteria were usually underwritten and often securitized by other market actors,
22:852:68588:16:17:89:522:325:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:such as banks. We analyze borrowers receiving both types of private modifications using
22:853:68675:17:16:89:522:308:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the JPMCI bank dataset described in Section 2.2. This includes both GSE and non-GSE
22:854:68758:16:17:89:522:292:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers whose mortgages are serviced by Chase and hence were eligible either for a pri-
22:855:68847:17:16:89:522:275:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:vate modification designed by the GSEs or a private modification designed by Chase. As
22:856:68933:16:16:89:504:259:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:we describe below, the GSE modification and the Chase modification are quite similar.
22:857:69018:16:17:106:522:243:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The design of HAMP and the private modifications we study reflect di-erent views
22:858:69098:17:16:89:522:226:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f17:B:about the most e-ective way to reduce defaults. HAMP was designed with an explicit31%
22:859:69183:16:17:89:523:210:119:g_d0_f17:119:g_d0_f4:B:payment-to-income (PTI) ratio target,as we mention in Section 3.1.This target evolved
22:860:69268:17:16:89:522:193:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:from the National Housing Act of 1937, which established a PTI limit in the federal govern-
22:861:69359:16:17:89:522:177:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ment’s public housing program. Adopting this income ratio target in a modification program
22:862:69449:17:16:89:522:160:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:assumes that borrowers with high PTI ratios must need much larger payment reductions in
22:863:69536:16:16:89:434:144:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:order to avoid subsequent default than borrowers with lower PTI ratios.
22:864:69607:16:17:106:523:128:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The first important feature of these private modification programs is that, in contrast
22:865:69694:17:16:89:522:111:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f17:B:to the rigid Payment-to-Income (PTI) ratio target in HAMP, they use apayment-reduction
22:866:69780:16:16:89:522:95:119:g_d0_f17:119:g_d0_f4:B:target.29Under this alternative view, the amount of payment reduction relative to the status
22:867:69872:16:0:98:522:79:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:29Chase private modifications target a 30 percent payment reduction.  GSE private modifications did
23:868:69973:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:quo is at least as important for reducing defaults as ensuring that the new payment is an
23:869:70062:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:“a-ordable” share of income according to the government’s metric. For borrowers with PTI
23:870:70150:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:near the 31 percent target, private modifications result in immediate payment reductions
23:871:70238:17:16:89:223:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that are larger than HAMP.
23:872:70264:16:17:106:523:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The second important feature of these private modification programs is that they use
23:873:70348:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:maturity extension as a low-cost tool for achieving deeper immediate payment reductions
23:874:70435:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:without reducing long-term obligations.  A range of contract terms can be modified in
23:875:70520:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:order to achieve a given amount of immediate payment reduction. As described in Section
23:876:70607:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:3.1, HAMP reduces payments by first providing interest rate reductions, then maturity
23:877:70692:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:extensions, and finally principal forbearance as necessary to achieve the 31 percent PTI ratio
23:878:70786:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:target. In contrast, the private modifications we study target larger payment reductions
23:879:70874:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:by first extending maturity and amortization terms (which we call maturity extension for
23:880:70962:17:16:89:523:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:simplicity).  In this way, deeper immediate payment reductions are o-set by continued
23:881:71047:16:17:89:218:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payments in the long-term.
23:882:71073:17:16:106:523:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Both of these distinctive features are visible in Figure 4 for Chase private modifications,
23:883:71164:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:which is our preferred estimation sample. (The modification design and point estimates for
23:884:71254:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:GSE private modifications are very similar, but the regression discontinuity design has a
23:885:71343:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:technical issue which we discuss later in this section.) This figure summarizes payments
23:886:71431:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:under each program using the same plot structure as Figure 1. Figure 4a shows the annual
23:887:71519:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:path of payments relative to the status quo for government and private modifications o-ered
23:888:71610:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to borrowers with PTI close to 31 percent.  Government (HAMP) modifications for this
23:889:71694:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sample have a modest reduction in payments until year 27, with small increases thereafter.
23:890:71784:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Private modifications lead to deeper payment reductions for the first 22 years and then to
23:891:71874:16:17:89:300:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:higher payments for the remaining 18 years.
23:892:71917:17:16:106:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Figure 4b shows that compared to government modifications, private modifications o-er
23:893:72002:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a relative reduction in immediate mortgage payments but leave the NPV of total payments
23:894:72089:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:owed approximately unchanged. This analysis uses the same methodology as in Section 3.1.
23:895:72177:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:The main force driving the deeper payment reductions is maturity extension, and when the
23:896:72265:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:discount rate equals the interest rate (consistent with the empirical evidence of borrower
23:897:72355:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:behavior in Busse et al. 2013), this results in no change in the NPV of total payments owed.
23:898:72447:17:16:89:522:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Because the private modification has deeper payment reductions for 22 years, it may be
23:899:72533:16:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:NPV-positive from the perspective of a more impatient borrower. Even for such borrowers,
23:900:72621:16:17:89:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:we attribute the causal impact of the private modification to its liquidity component because
23:901:72714:17:16:89:466:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in Section 3 we find that future mortgage payments do not a-ect default rates.
23:902:72792:16:20:106:522:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The mix of other modification characteristics also changed at the cuto-, though these
23:903:72877:20:11:89:522:130:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:not have a single payment reduction target, but Farrell et al. (2017) show that the GSE program e-ectively
23:904:72983:11:11:89:522:119:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:targeted a payment reduction of about 25 percent. While the HAMP program ended in December 2016, both
23:905:73084:11:11:89:522:108:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the Chase and GSE modification programs described in this section are ongoing and their rules are subject to
23:906:73192:11:11:89:522:97:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:change. Our description of the programs reflects guidelines in place during our analysis period. See Cowley
23:907:73299:11:0:89:506:86:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:(2017) for more detail about the evolution of private modifications across di-erent market participants.
24:908:73405:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:changes roughly o-set. As shown in the figure, borrowers receiving private modifications
24:909:73493:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:had less principal reduction.  This is because private modifications are ineligible for the
24:910:73584:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:subsidized principal reduction in HAMP.30On the other hand, private modifications had
24:911:73669:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:more principal forbearance and slightly deeper interest rate reductions, o-setting the e-ect
24:912:73761:16:23:89:367:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of reduced principal forgiveness from an NPV perspective.
24:913:73818:23:17:89:522:620:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:F:5.2  Identification: Discontinuity in Payment Reduction at the 31 percent
24:914:73891:17:26:119:271:603:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:Payment-to-Income Ratio
24:915:73914:26:17:106:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We use variation generated by HAMP’s 31 percent PTI eligibility cuto-and the di-erent
24:916:73999:17:16:89:522:560:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payment reduction targets used in HAMP and the private modification program.  Since
24:917:74082:16:17:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP was designed to reduce monthly payments to 31 percent of a borrower’s income,
24:918:74164:17:16:89:522:527:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers whose PTI ratio was already below 31 percent were ineligible for HAMP. These
24:919:74250:16:16:89:357:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers were only evaluated for private modifications.
24:920:74306:16:17:106:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The di-erence in modification program rules generates substantial variation in the
24:921:74388:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:amount of immediate payment reduction received by borrowers on either side of HAMP’s 31
24:922:74475:16:17:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:percent PTI eligibility cuto-. Below the cuto-, all borrowers receive private modifications
24:923:74566:17:16:89:522:445:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:with large payment reductions. Above the cuto-about half of borrowers receive HAMP
24:924:74648:16:17:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications with small payment reductions (since these borrowers are already close to
24:925:74735:17:16:89:522:412:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP’s 31 percent PTI target) and about half receive private modifications with large
24:926:74820:16:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payment reductions (since Chase had a minimum 30 percent payment reduction target).
24:927:74903:16:17:89:523:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Although borrowers above the cuto-who receive HAMP modifications with a 31 percent
24:928:74985:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:PTI ratio target would have received larger payment reductions in the private program,
24:929:75071:16:17:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP rules prohibited servicers from o-ering private sector alternatives to any HAMP-
24:930:75156:17:16:89:522:330:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:eligible borrower, under the assumption that private modifications would not be as e-ective
24:931:75247:16:17:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:as those subsidized by the government. Thus the only borrowers above the cuto-receiving
24:932:75334:17:16:89:522:297:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:private modifications are those failing to meet one of the other eligibility criteria described
24:933:75429:16:17:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in Section 3.1. The eligibility cuto-therefore serves as an instrument for borrowers moved
24:934:75519:17:16:89:522:264:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:from HAMP modifications with small payment reductions to private modifications with
24:935:75602:16:16:89:212:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:large payment reductions.
24:936:75627:16:17:106:523:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We make three sample restrictions for ease of exposition, though our central result is
24:937:75713:17:16:89:522:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:unchanged when we lift all three restrictions. First, to focus on a subsample eligible for
24:938:75803:16:17:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the full maturity extension treatment, we subset to mortgages whose current terms are less
24:939:75893:17:16:89:522:182:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:than or equal to 30 years. This maintains 87 percent of the sample. Second, to simplify the
24:940:75984:16:17:89:522:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:calculation of expected payments before and after modification in Section 6.2.1, we restrict
24:941:76076:17:16:89:522:149:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to fixed rate mortgages. This maintains 48 percent of observations.31Finally, we drop 254
24:942:76165:16:14:98:522:133:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:30As we discuss above, because we found no independent impact of principal reductions on default in
24:943:76264:14:11:89:522:119:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:Section 3.3, we attribute the causal impact of this treatment on default to the immediate payment reduction
24:944:76371:11:11:89:522:108:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:portion of the treatment.  In Section 5.3 we provide a bound on our estimate of the e-ect of payment
24:945:76471:11:7:89:505:97:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:reduction under the alternative assumption that the principal increase actually had an o-setting e-ect.
24:946:76574:7:15:98:522:90:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:31Although these sample restrictions drop a substantial share of observations within our sample, they keep
24:947:76680:15:0:89:522:75:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the type of mortgages that were most prevalent during this time period. As a result, these restrictions make
25:948:76790:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:observations between 31 percent and 31.1 percent PTI who receive an amount of payment
25:949:76875:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction about halfway between that received by borrowers clearly above and clearly below
25:950:76965:16:17:89:138:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the cuto-.
25:951:76975:17:16:106:523:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We provide the same tests as for our prior principal reduction regression discontinuity
25:952:77062:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:strategy. Table 1b shows that borrowers in our sample are broadly representative of un-
25:953:77149:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:derwater delinquent borrowers during the recent crisis and similar on observables to the
25:954:77237:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction sample. Online Appendix Figure 12 shows that predicted default rates
25:955:77325:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:based on pre-determined covariates trend smoothly through the cuto-. We provide addi-
25:956:77410:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:tional detail on covariate balance in online Appendix B.2.1. Finally, online Appendix Figure
25:957:77502:16:23:89:399:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:13 shows that borrower density is also smooth around the cuto-.
25:958:77565:23:27:89:409:538:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:5.3  Results: E-ect of Payment Reduction on Default
25:959:77616:27:16:106:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Figure 5a shows that borrowers below the cuto-receive payment reductions that are

25:975:78635:17:16:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:bank dataset. The sample includes borrowers with PTI ratios between 25 and 80 who we
25:976:78719:16:17:89:522:249:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:observe for at least two years after modification.33For symmetry around the 31 percent

25:985:79403:7:15:98:522:112:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:32Online Appendix Figure 14 reports conditional means with respect to the running variable for the change
25:986:79508:15:7:89:506:97:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:in the NPV of payments owed, the amount of principal forgiveness, and the change in the interest rate.
25:987:79610:7:14:98:522:90:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:33Borrower density thins out above PTI ratios of 80, and borrowers with PTI ratios below 25 are evaluated
25:988:79715:14:0:89:237:76:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:according to di-erent program rules.
26:989:79753:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cuto-. Second, the slope of the estimated default rates in the bottom panel mirrors the slope
26:990:79846:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of the payment reductions in the top panel; default rates are approximately constant on the
26:991:79937:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:left-hand side of the cuto-, consistent with a constant amount of payment reduction, and
26:992:80025:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:are falling on the right-hand side of the cuto-, consistent with a rising amount of payment
26:993:80116:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction. This pattern is even more striking in online Appendix Figure 15, which plots the
26:994:80207:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:first stage and reduced form for borrowers with PTI ratios all the way out to 80 percent.
26:995:80296:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Our point estimate ofˆ·from equation 4 is that an extra one percent payment reduction
26:996:80381:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduces default rates in the two years after modification by 0.34 percentage point, or by 1.1
26:997:80474:16:16:89:268:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:percent of the mean above the cuto-.
26:998:80510:16:17:106:522:561:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f4:A:Robustness –Online Appendix Figure 15 shows that when we remove all three of the
26:999:80590:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sample restrictions described above we find an extra one percent payment reduction reduces
26:1000:80680:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:default rates by 0.26 percentage point. This reduction is 0.95 percent of the default rate
26:1001:80770:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:above the cuto-, which is similar to our estimate of 1.1 percent in the baseline sample.
26:1002:80858:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Online Appendix Figure 16 shows that our estimates are stable for a variety of alternative
26:1003:80948:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:bandwidths. Our point estimate is similar (rising to 1.3 percent) if we use the upper bound
26:1004:81039:16:16:89:523:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of our confidence interval from Section 3.3 to adjust for any potential e-ect of the relative
26:1005:81132:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:increase in mortgage principal at the cuto-.  Online Appendix B.2.1 provides additional
26:1006:81219:17:16:89:210:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:detail on this calculation.
26:1007:81246:16:17:106:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We also analyze the e-ects of immediate payment reduction for GSE-backed loans and
26:1008:81328:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:find a similar reduction in delinquency. For borrowers ineligible for HAMP, the GSEs o-ered
26:1009:81419:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a private modification that was very similar to the Chase private modification in that it
26:1010:81508:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:featured a payment reduction target and for most borrowers used maturity extensions prior
26:1011:81597:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to any interest rate reduction. Borrowers on the left-hand side receive payment reductions
26:1012:81687:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that are 22.4 percentage points more generous than borrowers on the right-hand side and
26:1013:81774:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:have default rates that are 6.1 percentage points lower.34We estimate that a one percent
26:1014:81862:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction in payments reduces default by 0.27 percentage point.  This reduction is 1.0
26:1015:81948:17:16:89:523:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:percent of the default rate above the cuto-, which is similar to our estimate of a reduction
26:1016:82040:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of 1.1 percent for non-GSE loans. It is reassuring that we recover essentially the same point
26:1017:82133:17:16:89:395:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:estimate when using a completely di-erent sample of borrowers.
26:1018:82195:16:17:106:523:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:However, the research design for the GSE-backed loans does not pass one of the standard
26:1019:82282:17:16:89:522:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:RD identification checks and hence it is not our preferred specification. There are more
26:1020:82370:16:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers on theright-handside of the cuto-than on the left-hand side, as shown in online
26:1021:82459:16:17:89:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Appendix Figure 20. This issue does not arise because of borrower manipulation of PTI,
26:1022:82545:17:16:89:522:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:which would induce more mass on theleft-handside where additional payment reduction
26:1023:82628:16:15:98:522:150:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:34The sample of GSE modifications covers the same 2011 through 2016 time period as the sample of Chase
26:1024:82730:15:10:89:522:135:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:modifications. Online Appendix Figures 17, 18, 19 and 20 replicate our 31 percent PTI cuto-analysis for
26:1025:82833:10:11:89:522:125:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the GSE-backed loans sample. Recall that in online Appendix Figure 14 we showed that there was no change
26:1026:82937:11:11:89:522:114:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:in NPV of payments owed at the cuto-for the non-GSE-backed sample because more interest rate reduction
26:1027:83039:11:11:89:522:103:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:was o-set by less principal reduction. Fannie Mae and Freddie Mac did not allow principal forgiveness (even
26:1028:83146:11:11:89:522:92:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:for HAMP recipients) and so in the GSE-backed sample the reduction in the NPV of payments owed is
26:1029:83243:11:0:89:213:81:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:smaller on the right-hand side.
27:1030:83276:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:is available. Rather, it arises because eligibility for GSE private modifications required a
27:1031:83368:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:FICO lower than 620 for borrowers less than 60 days delinquent at the time of modification,
27:1032:83459:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:while HAMP had no such screen. As a result, there is an imbalance where the left-hand side
27:1033:83549:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:has no less than 60 days delinquent borrowers with FICO above 620 and the right-hand side
27:1034:83638:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:has borrowers of all FICO scores and pre-modification delinquency statuses. We are unable
27:1035:83727:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to correct this problem because we do not observe FICO in the JPMCI data. Nevertheless,
27:1036:83814:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:we believe the bias from these extra low-delinquency higher FICO borrowers is small and
27:1037:83901:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:therefore find this research design to still be informative.35Thus, we find that payment
27:1038:83989:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction as implemented through both the Chase and GSE private alternatives to HAMP
27:1039:84073:16:28:89:438:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:has a substantial e-ect on default for a wide range of types of borrowers.
27:1040:84147:28:30:89:264:533:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:6  Implications: Default
27:1041:84171:30:17:106:523:503:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In this section we discuss the positive and normative implications of our results on de-
27:1042:84259:17:16:89:522:486:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:fault.  Our finding that default is responsive to immediate payment reductions but not
27:1043:84345:16:16:89:522:470:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:long-term principal reduction provides support for liquidity-driven theories of default. Be-
27:1044:84437:16:17:89:522:454:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cause liquidity is the main driver of borrower default decisions, we show that maturity
27:1045:84524:17:16:89:522:437:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:extensions as implemented at the HAMP cuto-can provide deeper payment reductions and
27:1046:84608:16:17:89:522:421:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduced default rates in a way that leaves borrowers, lenders, and taxpayers better o-. This
27:1047:84700:17:16:89:522:404:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:result can be used to draw lessons for the e-cient structure of mortgage modifications in a
27:1048:84791:16:20:89:148:388:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:future crisis.
27:1049:84805:20:26:89:319:368:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:6.1  Positive: Liquidity Drives Default
27:1050:84844:26:17:106:523:342:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our empirical results show that immediate liquidity substantially a-ects borrower de-
27:1051:84929:17:16:89:522:325:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:fault decisions but that reductions in mortgage principal do not. This suggests that, at least
27:1052:85023:16:17:89:522:309:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:for our sample, immediate liquidity is the main driver of borrower default. This contrasts
27:1053:85113:17:16:89:444:292:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:with strategic default explanations based on the degree of negative equity.
27:1054:85188:16:17:106:522:276:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Indeed, quantitatively our results suggest thatimmediateliquidity provision is a key
27:1055:85272:17:16:89:523:259:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:driver of the default reductions found in two types of prior work analyzing the e-ect of
27:1056:85360:16:16:89:523:243:119:g_d0_f17:119:g_d0_f4:B:sustainedpayment reductions. First, Agarwal et al. (2011) and Haughwout et al. (2016)
27:1057:85445:16:17:89:522:227:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:analyze modifications provided to delinquent borrowers before the implementation of the
27:1058:85532:17:16:89:522:210:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP program.  They find that a one percent immediate payment reduction that also
27:1059:85613:16:17:89:522:194:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduces long-term debt obligations is associated with a 1.1 percent to 1.3 percent reduction
27:1060:85705:17:16:89:522:177:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in default rates.36Second, other authors have analyzed the e-ect of sustained payment
27:1061:85790:16:14:98:522:161:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:35Two pieces of evidence suggest the bias is small. First, we plot predicted delinquency as a function of
27:1062:85895:14:11:89:522:147:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:average observable borrower characteristics in online Appendix Figure 19. There is little change in predicted
27:1063:86004:11:11:89:522:136:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:delinquency at the cuto-. Second, the extra borrowers on the right-hand side are more creditworthy. This
27:1064:86108:11:11:89:522:125:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:change in sample composition will lower average default rates on the right-hand side, leading us to understate
27:1065:86218:11:7:89:245:114:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the e-ectiveness of payment reduction.
27:1066:86256:7:15:98:522:107:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:36In addition, Agarwal et al. (2017a) show that HAMP modifications with both short and long-term
27:1067:86352:15:11:89:522:92:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:payment reduction led to significant reductions in default rates, though they do not estimate an elasticity
27:1068:86459:11:0:89:310:81:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:with respect to a given quantity of payment reduction.
28:1069:86515:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reductions for non-distressed borrowers. Although di-erences in borrower characteristics
28:1070:86603:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and baseline default rates makes it di-cult to directly compare magnitudes between dis-
28:1071:86690:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:tressed and non-distressed borrowers, this literature has found that a one percent payment
28:1072:86780:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction is associated with a 0.8 percent to 2.0 percent reduction in default rates.37The
28:1073:86870:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:similarity between our estimates of the e-ect of immediate payment reduction and those of
28:1074:86959:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the prior literature analyzing the e-ect of sustained payment reductions suggests that imme-
28:1075:87051:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:diate liquidity provision is a main driver of the default reductions documented in previous
28:1076:87142:17:16:89:115:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:work.
28:1077:87147:16:16:106:523:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:These empirical results provide support for double-trigger theories of mortgage default,
28:1078:87235:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in which households default when they are underwaterandface a liquidity shock. Negative
28:1079:87322:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:equity is a necessary condition for default because households with positive equity can
28:1080:87409:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrow to make payments or sell the house to avoid foreclosure. However it is not generally
28:1081:87500:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a su-cient condition for default because there is option value to staying in a mortgage and
28:1082:87591:16:17:89:275:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:because default is costly for borrowers.
28:1083:87631:17:16:106:523:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:For example, Campbell and Cocco (2015) develop a calibrated model and find that in
28:1084:87713:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a baseline case with cost-less default the relationship between leverage and default is flat
28:1085:87805:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:until about 135 LTV. Our empirical evidence suggests that default is insensitive to LTVs
28:1086:87893:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:even at slightly higher LTV ratios, which is consistent with adding a utility cost of default
28:1087:87986:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to this type of model (we show this formally in online Appendix D.3).38The result that
28:1088:88072:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers without liquidity shocks do not exercise their default option until substantially
28:1089:88163:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:underwater is consistent with empirical evidence in Bhutta et al. (2017), who show that the
28:1090:88254:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:median homeowner without a liquidity shock does not default until their LTV is greater
28:1091:88340:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:than 174, while the result that default jumps once borrowers are moved from positive to
28:1092:88427:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:negative equity is consistent with the result in Gupta and Hansman (2018), who find that
28:1093:88515:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:debt increases lead to increased defaults for option ARM borrowers who start with positive
28:1094:88605:16:16:89:121:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:equity.
28:1095:88612:16:15:98:522:282:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:37See Tracy and Wright (2012), Fuster and Willen (2017), and DiMaggio et al. (2017).  These papers
28:1096:88710:15:11:89:523:267:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:analyze the e-ect of payment reductions caused by downward adjustments of interest rates for borrowers
28:1097:88812:11:11:89:522:256:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:with adjustable rate mortgages.  As Fuster and Willen (2017) discuss, to the extent that borrowers are
28:1098:88914:11:11:89:522:245:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:aware of their mortgage terms and follow the movement of underlying index rates, then these estimates
28:1099:89015:11:11:89:522:234:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:may already be capturing only the liquidity e-ects of lower payments since borrowers would already have
28:1100:89118:11:11:89:522:223:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:been anticipating and responding to the long-term payment reductions. Similarly, Scharlemann and Shore
28:1101:89220:11:11:89:522:212:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:(2017) analyze the e-ect of sustained payment increases for non-distressed borrowers in a setting where these
28:1102:89329:11:11:89:522:201:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:payment increases are pre-determined five years ahead of time (resulting from a step up in interest rates as
28:1103:89437:11:11:89:522:190:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:part of a previous mortgage modification). The four aforementioned papers capture the e-ect of payments
28:1104:89540:11:11:89:522:179:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:on default for the average borrower. Other work looking at the e-ect for borrowers that choose to refinance
28:1105:89647:11:7:89:433:168:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:by Ehrlich and Perry (2015) and Abel and Fuster (2018) has found larger elasticities.
28:1106:89732:7:0:98:469:161:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:?:38The 90th percentile LTV in our principal reduction regression discontinuity sample is 163.
29:1107:89826:0:27:89:259:709:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:6.2  Normative Implications
29:1108:89853:27:16:89:543:682:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f28:C:6.2.1  Can Maturity Extension Reduce Defaults While Leaving Borrowers, Lenders,
29:1109:89932:16:27:127:270:666:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f28:C:and Taxpayers Better o-?
29:1110:89956:27:16:106:523:639:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Since the amount of liquidity provision appears more important than the way that liq-
29:1111:90041:16:16:89:522:623:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:uidity is provided, our results imply that maturity-extension-financed payment reduction
29:1112:90129:16:17:89:522:607:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:may generate a Pareto improvement, leaving borrowers, lenders, and taxpayers all better
29:1113:90216:17:16:89:523:590:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:o-. To understand why this is true, it is useful to revisit the particular structure of mortgage
29:1114:90312:16:17:89:522:574:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications around the HAMP eligibility discontinuity we study in Section 5. A borrower
29:1115:90401:17:16:89:522:557:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:who moves from the right-hand side of the cuto-(“control”) to the left-hand side (“treat-
29:1116:90490:16:17:89:522:541:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ment”) sees deeper immediate payment reductions that are o-set by continued payments in
29:1117:90577:17:16:89:522:524:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the long-term. Intuitively, maturity extension is equivalent to the lender “lending” the bor-
29:1118:90670:16:17:89:522:508:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rower their monthly payment reductions at the mortgage interest rate, with repayments on
29:1119:90758:17:16:89:522:491:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:this “new” loan beginning at the end of the original mortgage term and continuing through
29:1120:90847:16:16:89:231:475:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the end of the new loan term.
29:1121:90876:16:17:106:523:459:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:For borrowers, a maturity extension which moves funds from the future to the present
29:1122:90960:17:16:89:522:442:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:might be particularly valuable in periods of acute economic distress.  In our setting, all
29:1123:91050:16:17:89:522:426:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers are better o-in the treatment group under relatively mild assumptions about
29:1124:91135:17:16:89:522:409:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:monotonicity and revealed preference. Borrowers can be divided into four potential groups:
29:1125:91225:16:17:89:522:393:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:those who default under both contracts, those who switch from defaulting to paying on
29:1126:91310:17:16:89:522:376:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:schedule, those who switch from paying on schedule to defaulting, and those who pay on
29:1127:91396:16:16:89:522:360:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:schedule under either contract. The first group defaults under both contracts and is therefore
29:1128:91490:16:17:89:522:344:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:no worse o-receiving treatment. The second group is better o-because they indicate by
29:1129:91575:17:16:89:522:327:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:revealed preference that the modified loan is more attractive than defaulting. If we assume
29:1130:91666:16:17:89:522:311:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that default is monotonically decreasing with the extent of payment reduction–the canonical
29:1131:91757:17:16:89:522:294:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:assumption from Imbens and Angrist (1994) needed to identify a local average treatment
29:1132:91843:16:17:89:523:278:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:e-ect–then there is no one in the third group. Finally, the fourth group is better o-because
29:1133:91935:17:16:89:522:261:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:their choice set is expanded; they always have the choice to ignore the maturity extension
29:1134:92025:16:17:89:306:245:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:and repay the loan on the original schedule.39
29:1135:92071:17:16:106:523:228:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:For lenders, a maturity extension will increase the NPV of total payments owed when the
29:1136:92158:16:16:89:522:212:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:mortgage’s interest rate is higher than the lender’s current discount rate. In this time period
29:1137:92253:16:17:89:522:196:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the interest rates on new mortgages were a few percentage points below the average interest
29:1138:92344:17:16:89:522:179:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rate on existing mortgages. Hence, when using current interest rates as a measure of the
29:1139:92432:16:17:89:522:163:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:opportunity cost of capital, extending maturities on existing mortgages would increase the
29:1140:92522:17:16:89:522:146:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:NPV of payments owed to the lender. Although most of the incremental payment reduction
29:1141:92608:16:17:89:522:130:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:at the cuto-we study was achieved from maturity extension, part came from interest rate
29:1142:92695:17:15:89:522:113:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction, which reduces the NPV of payments owed.  This works against the maturity
29:1143:92778:15:15:98:522:98:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:39Borrowers who recently defaulted on their mortgage are likely to want liquidity and so a low-interest
29:1144:92881:15:11:89:522:83:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:loan is likely to be attractive. Relatedly, Argyle et al. (2017) have shown that there is strong consumer
29:1145:92986:11:0:89:314:72:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:demand for extended maturity in the auto loan market.
30:1146:93041:0:17:89:165:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:extension e-ect.
30:1147:93057:17:16:106:523:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In our setting, we find that the NPV of the payments owed under the contract is similar
30:1148:93144:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in the treatment and control group. To be specific, online Appendix Figure 14 shows that
30:1149:93232:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:treatment lowers NPV by $2,860 relative to the control group when lenders use a 4.11 percent
