30:1150:93324:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:discount rate, which is the average of the 30-year mortgage rate during our sample period.
30:1151:93414:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:This is a modest loss and with a standard error of $2,025 we are unable to statistically
30:1152:93502:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reject that there is no change in the NPV to lenders (consistent with the criteria for a
30:1153:93590:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Pareto improvement). This estimate–which assumes that all borrowers repay on schedule–
30:1154:93676:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:has three shortcomings:  some borrowers default (and treatment reduces default), some
30:1155:93761:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers prepay their mortgage, and lenders may discount cash flows after year 30 at a
30:1156:93848:17:16:89:275:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:higher rate than short-term cash flows.
30:1157:93887:16:17:106:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:To address these limitations, we build anexpected paymentsNPV model and find that
30:1158:93968:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:under plausible assumptions lenders are better o-assigning a borrower to treatment. We
30:1159:94054:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:proceed in three steps. First, we incorporate default by using our causal estimate of the
30:1160:94143:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:e-ect of treatment on default.40We combine this with prior evidence on the losses incurred
30:1161:94233:16:16:89:523:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:by lenders when borrowers default.41Because treatment significantly reduces default rates,
30:1162:94323:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:this moves the lender to a gain of $8,301. Second, the fact that the payments arrive further
30:1163:94415:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in the future means that we need to use a higher discount rate, which decreases the NPV.
30:1164:94503:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:We estimate a term premium of 32 basis points between 30- and 40-year mortgages by
30:1165:94585:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:extrapolating from observed mortgage rates (see online Appendix Figure 21), which shrinks
30:1166:94674:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the gain to the lender to $5,279. Finally, we incorporate realistic prepayment behavior for
30:1167:94765:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a final estimate of $5,350. We provide more detail on this calculation as well as several
30:1168:94854:16:16:89:282:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:robustness checks in online Appendix C.
30:1169:94893:16:17:106:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The finding that lenders are better o-from maturity extensions depends on two crucial
30:1170:94978:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:assumptions.  First, we assume that prevailing mortgage interest rates accurately reflect
30:1171:95067:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a lender’s opportunity cost of capital.  But if some lenders are liquidity-constrained (as
30:1172:95157:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:might be implied by the fall in mortgage originations during this time period), then market
30:1173:95248:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rates for those borrowers who can get a mortgage might not reflect a lender’s true cost of
30:1174:95338:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:capital.42We calculate that a lender is better o-from treatment as long as her discount rate
30:1175:95430:16:16:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:is below 6.02 percent. Second, we assume that implied mortgage spreads accurately capture
30:1176:95519:16:15:98:523:216:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:40Using our causal estimate of the e-ect of treatment implicitly assumes that maturity extension does not
30:1177:95624:15:11:89:522:201:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:raise defaults outside of the time horizon we observe in the data. This assumption could fail because maturity
30:1178:95734:11:11:89:522:190:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:extension slows the repayment of principal and higher LTVs might raise long-term default rates. However,
30:1179:95838:11:11:89:522:179:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:this higher LTV e-ect should be weighed against the e-ect of maturity extension on mortgage payments,
30:1180:95939:11:11:89:522:168:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:which are still lower on average 22 years after modification. After 22 years, all borrowers will have regained
30:1181:96049:11:7:89:522:157:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:positive home equity. It is thus likely that foreclosures are permanently lower under this modification type.
30:1182:96158:7:15:98:522:150:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:41Defaults impose losses on lenders both because the house is underwater and because foreclosed homes
30:1183:96259:15:11:89:522:135:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:sell at a discount relative to their market value. We assume that a foreclosure or short sale causes a lender
30:1184:96368:11:10:89:522:124:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:loss equal to 56 percent of the unpaid balance of the loan, equal to the losses experienced by Fannie Mae
30:1185:96473:10:11:89:522:114:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:on foreclosures and short sales in 2011 (Fannie Mae 2018). In the online Appendix C, we show that our
30:1186:96574:11:11:89:523:103:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:conclusion that lenders are not measurably worse o-in terms of expected payments is robust to alternative
30:1187:96679:11:8:89:335:92:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:assumptions about the lender’s recovery rate on foreclosures.
30:1188:96740:8:0:98:488:84:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:?:42Online Appendix Figure 22a shows the time series of mortgage originations during this period.
31:1189:96837:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the lender’s disutility from extending the mortgage term from 30 to 40 years.  Because
31:1190:96923:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of uncertainty over this spread, we show that our results are robust to using a variety of
31:1191:97013:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:term premium assumptions in online Appendix C. However, the term premium we use in
31:1192:97095:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:our baseline case (32 basis points) is already significantly higher than the actual 30- to
31:1193:97185:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:40-year spread for swaps and corporate bonds in our sample period (two and nine basis
31:1194:97270:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:points, respectively). Furthermore, the flat swap yield curve during this time period implies
31:1195:97363:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that a lender concerned about increased portfolio duration risk from extending mortgage
31:1196:97450:17:16:89:358:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:maturities could hedge this risk at low incremental cost.
31:1197:97507:16:16:106:523:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Finally, taxpayers are also better o-from more maturity extensions. The government
31:1198:97589:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:spent substantial resources subsidizing HAMP modifications above the eligibility cuto-with
31:1199:97679:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:small payment reductions and high default rates, whereas lenders were willing to provide
31:1200:97767:16:17:89:523:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers below the cuto-private modifications requiring no government assistance which
31:1201:97854:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:had large payment reductions and low default rates.  This suggests that using maturity
31:1202:97940:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:extensions as the first step in modifying mortgages could have saved substantial taxpayer
31:1203:98029:17:16:89:134:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:subsidies.
31:1204:98039:16:16:106:523:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Indeed, our results raise concerns that HAMP’s structure led to the crowding out of al-
31:1205:98126:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ternative private modifications that would have led to lower defaults while saving taxpayer
31:1206:98217:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:money. The 31 percent PTI target in HAMP means that borrowers with pre-modification
31:1207:98300:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:PTI ratios below 42 percent received payment reductionssmallerthan the 30 percent pay-
31:1208:98386:17:16:89:523:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ment reductions o-ered in private modifications. For these borrowers, an alternative private
31:1209:98478:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:bilateral modification program such as the ones we study would have resulted in more gener-
31:1210:98569:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ous immediate payment reduction and, according to our empirical results, lower default rates
31:1211:98661:16:16:89:523:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:without requiring any government subsidy.43About 40 percent of all borrowers with HAMP
31:1212:98747:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications (625,000 borrowers) were in this region, and the government spent approx-
31:1213:98834:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:imately $7 billion subsidizing potentially less e-ective modifications for these borrowers.
31:1214:98925:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Furthermore, the government explicitly prohibited servicers from o-ering alternative pri-
31:1215:99014:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:vate modifications to any HAMP-eligible borrower under the (incorrect) assumption that
31:1216:99100:16:17:89:523:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the private modifications would not be as e-ective as those subsidized by the government.
31:1217:99189:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Our data on private modifications and the HAMP-first requirement indicate that HAMP
31:1218:99272:16:17:89:523:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:crowded out private modifications that could have been more e-ective for a large fraction
31:1219:99361:17:15:89:293:215:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:of borrowers in the government program.44
31:1220:99402:15:15:98:522:200:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:43The results are likely to extend to non-GSE and non-Chase borrowers.  Averaging over all private
31:1221:99500:15:11:89:523:185:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:modifications, the average payment reduction was around 20% (O-ce of the Comptroller of the Currency
31:1222:99600:11:11:89:522:174:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:2012), which suggests that the private sector was willing to facilitate substantial payment reductions in
31:1223:99705:11:11:89:522:163:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the absence of HAMP subsidies. On the other hand, Agarwal et al. (2017a) show that there is important
31:1224:99806:11:7:89:402:152:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:variation across servicers in their capacity to execute mortgage modifications.
31:1225:99885:7:15:98:522:145:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:44While our emphasis is on crowd-out on the intensive margin of the quality of modifications, Agarwal
31:1226:99986:15:11:89:522:130:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:et al. (2017a) provide evidence on the extensive margin in terms of the quantity of modifications. They
31:1227:100089:11:11:89:522:119:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:show that each HAMP modification is associated with about 0.84 more “net” modifications, suggesting
31:1228:100188:11:11:89:522:108:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:that the program did not substantially reduce the total number of private modifications that would have
31:1229:100291:11:11:89:523:97:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:been o-ered in the absence of the program.  They argue that by inducing more borrowers to apply for
31:1230:100390:11:11:89:522:86:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:modifications, HAMP increased the private modification rate of HAMP-ineligible borrowers, o-setting the
31:1231:100493:11:0:89:522:75:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:reduced private modification rate of HAMP-eligible borrowers. Our evidence suggests that at least some of
32:1232:100600:0:17:106:523:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our findings that payment reductions can be structured so as to reduce default rates
32:1233:100684:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:while leaving all parties better o-contrast sharply with our findings for principal reduction,
32:1234:100778:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:which was ine-ective even while being costly to both lenders and taxpayers. Future pri-
32:1235:100865:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:vate and public modification programs will have a menu of options for restructuring loans.
32:1236:100955:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Our findings suggest that among these options, those that maximize immediate payment
32:1237:101039:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction are likely to be most e-ective, and that maturity extension is a particular way
32:1238:101128:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to achieve large immediate payment reductions at little cost to lenders and taxpayers. We
32:1239:101217:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:explore the broader implications of these results for modification design in more detail in
32:1240:101308:16:22:89:168:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the next section.
32:1241:101325:22:27:89:398:555:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f28:C:6.2.2  E-cient Default-Minimizing Modification Design
32:1242:101378:27:16:106:523:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our empirical research designs capture the two extremes in the debate about mortgage
32:1243:101462:16:16:89:522:512:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification design. Recall from the introduction that Treasury Secretary Timothy Geith-
32:1244:101550:16:17:89:522:496:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ner has explained that the government’s “biggest debate was whether to try to reduce overall
32:1245:101642:17:16:89:522:479:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:mortgage loans or just monthly payments.” Our first research design captures the pole of
32:1246:101730:16:17:89:523:463:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:o-ering borrowers housing wealth by forgiving mortgage principal without any immediate
32:1247:101816:17:16:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:change in liquidity. The second captures the pole of o-ering borrowers liquidity with ap-
32:1248:101905:16:17:89:522:430:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:proximately no change in wealth. In fact, most of the 10 million government-subsidized and
32:1249:101995:17:16:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:private sector modifications completed during the Great Recession a-ected both liquidity
32:1250:102083:16:17:89:522:397:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and wealth. In this section, we explain how our results help to answer the question of how
32:1251:102173:17:16:89:523:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to e-ciently design mortgage modifications for all borrowers, and we quantify the potential
32:1252:102264:16:16:89:522:364:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:gains of implementing our proposed design relative to the mortgage modifications that were
32:1253:102354:16:17:89:171:348:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:actually pursued.
32:1254:102371:17:16:106:523:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our empirical findings that default is responsive to liquidity but not wealth suggest a
32:1255:102458:16:17:89:522:315:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:simple principle for reducing mortgage defaults: the “best” modification steps are those that
32:1256:102551:17:16:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:achieve immediate payment reduction at the lowest possible cost. The costs of payment
32:1257:102636:16:17:89:522:282:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reductions must be born by either lenders or taxpayers.  Minimizing costs per dollar of
32:1258:102723:17:16:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:immediate liquidity provision will maximize the amount of payment reduction (and hence
32:1259:102809:16:16:89:522:249:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:default reduction) that the market will find privately optimal to provide on its own and
32:1260:102897:16:17:89:522:233:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:identify the most e-cient use of government subsidies. Hence, we call modifications that
32:1261:102985:17:16:89:468:216:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:follow this minimum-cost structure “e-cient default-minimizing modifications.”
32:1262:103063:16:17:106:523:200:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:To uncover the e-cient default-minimizing structure of mortgage modifications we eval-
32:1263:103149:17:16:89:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:uate the five modification steps that were used in various combinations in the public and
32:1264:103238:16:17:89:522:167:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:private modification programs we are aware of: maturity extension, temporary five-year
32:1265:103324:17:16:89:522:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:interest rate reduction, principal forbearance, permanent interest rate reduction, and prin-
32:1266:103416:16:16:89:522:134:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cipal forgiveness. These policies all reduce mortgage payments for at least five years, but
32:1267:103507:16:20:89:523:118:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:have very di-erent costs.  We calculate these costs for an illustrative mortgage with the
32:1268:103596:20:11:89:522:98:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the borrowers pushed from private to HAMP modifications would have received larger payment reductions,
32:1269:103698:11:11:89:522:87:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:and had lower short-term default rates, if they had remained in private modifications designed to emphasize
32:1270:103805:11:0:89:310:76:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:payment reduction rather than an income-ratio target.
33:1271:103860:0:17:89:443:709:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:characteristics of the average loan at the HAMP eligibility discontinuity.45
33:1272:103936:17:16:106:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We rank modification steps by their cost-e-ectiveness in Figure 6a. We calculate the
33:1273:104020:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:change in mortgage terms needed to reduce payments by 10 percent and the change in the
33:1274:104106:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:NPV of payments owed to the lender from this modification step. We find that maturity
33:1275:104191:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:extension is NPV-positiveby nearly $20,000 for the lender because the interest rate on the
33:1276:104281:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:loan is higher than the lender’s discount rate (recall that interest rates on new mortgages
33:1277:104372:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:fell substantially during the crisis, so the spread between the old rate on the mortgage being
33:1278:104466:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modified and the available return on new mortgages widened).  Temporary interest rate
33:1279:104551:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reductions are NPV-negative, costing about $14,000, while principal forbearance, permanent
33:1280:104641:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rate reduction, and principal forgiveness are even more NPV-negative with costs between
33:1281:104728:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:$22,000 and $32,000. Figure 6a also shows that the same ranking of policies continues to
33:1282:104816:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:hold when we examine the change in the NPV of expected payments incorporating the
33:1283:104897:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:yield curve and the impact of modifications on default and prepayment risk.46Across all
33:1284:104984:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification steps we find that the costs to the lender are lower when we incorporate these
33:1285:105075:17:16:89:445:478:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:features and that the ranking from least cost to highest cost is the same.47
33:1286:105151:16:16:106:523:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We use this ranking to propose e-cient default-minimizing modifications for a range
33:1287:105234:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of payment reduction targets.  As we note above, by e-cient we mean that we use the
33:1288:105317:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:lowest-cost policies first. We assume there are limits to how much some mortgage terms can
33:1289:105407:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:plausibly change. For example, maturity extension cannot possibly reduce payments below
33:1290:105494:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the interest payments on the unpaid balance. We restrict the set of possible modifications
33:1291:105584:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:using the quantitative limits implemented by the HAMP, Chase, and GSE modification
33:1292:105666:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:programs: we allow for maturity extension up to 40 years, we allow temporary interest rates
33:1293:105757:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to be reduced to 2 percent and we allow permanent interest rates to be reduced to the
33:1294:105842:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:prevailing 30-year mortgage rate. Adopting these limits makes our characterization of the
33:1295:105931:17:16:89:485:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:potential gains from more e-ciently-designed mortgage modifications conservative.
33:1296:106012:16:17:106:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The e-cient default-minimizing modification uses maturity extension, followed by tem-
33:1297:106097:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:porary interest rate reduction, followed by principal forbearance, and never principal for-
33:1298:106188:16:16:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:giveness. In Figure 6b, we depict the cost of such a modification. Maturity extension can
33:1299:106277:16:15:98:522:249:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:45This loan has a 6.7 percent fixed interest rate, a 23-year remaining term, an unpaid balance of $248,000
33:1300:106383:15:7:89:251:234:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:and a loan-to-value ratio of 131 percent.
33:1301:106424:7:15:98:522:227:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:46We use the same assumptions to calculate expected payments NPV calculation as in Section 6.2.1. We
33:1302:106524:15:11:89:522:212:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:need one new assumption, which is a function that maps payment reduction to default rates for lower levels
33:1303:106630:11:11:89:522:201:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:of payment reduction. We extrapolate from our evidence on default rates and online Appendix Figure 23
33:1304:106731:11:7:89:167:190:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:shows the function.
33:1305:106750:7:15:98:522:183:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:47One limitation of this ranking is that it assumes that payment reduction over a five-year horizon is the
33:1306:106856:15:11:89:522:168:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:main driver of a policy’s e-ect on a loan’s lifetime default rate. Implicitly, we are assuming that payments
33:1307:106964:11:11:89:522:157:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:in the next five years are the relevant variable for the re-default probability of a borrower who is currently
33:1308:107074:11:11:89:522:146:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:in financial distress. This assumption could be wrong in either direction. On one hand, perhaps reducing
33:1309:107178:11:11:89:522:135:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:payments for one year or three years can deliver much of the same reduction in defaults with even less
33:1310:107280:11:10:89:522:124:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:cost. On the other hand, default could rise substantially when payments rise in year six, though empirical
33:1311:107386:10:11:89:522:114:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:evidence in Scharlemann and Shore 2017 shows that this e-ect is quantitatively small. A payment increase
33:1312:107490:11:11:89:522:103:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:of about 10 percent in year six raises the default rate in the following year from 3.8 percent to 4.6 percent.
33:1313:107600:11:11:89:522:92:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:Unfortunately, our empirical evidence does not speak to this question and we think that understanding the
33:1314:107705:11:0:89:415:81:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:optimal duration of payment reductions is an important area for future research.
34:1315:107787:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduce payments by up to 16 percent if the loan term is extended from 26 to 40 years, pay-
34:1316:107877:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ments can be reduced by an additional 41 percent by reducing the temporary interest rate
34:1317:107965:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to 2 percent, and forbearance can reduce payments even further.48The figure also shows
34:1318:108051:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the cost of principal forgiveness. Together these two lines show the envelope of the least
34:1319:108141:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and most costly ways to achieve various amounts of payment reduction and hence various
34:1320:108227:17:16:89:230:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:amounts of default reduction.
34:1321:108256:16:17:106:523:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The modification policies actually used during the crisis occupy an intermediate position
34:1322:108345:17:16:89:523:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:within the envelope of the most e-cient and least e-cient policies. Recall that HAMP tar-
34:1323:108434:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:gets a PTI ratio of 31 percent. This means that borrowers receive widely-varying amounts
34:1324:108522:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of payment reduction on the basis of their initial PTI ratio. As discussed in Section 3.1,
34:1325:108612:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP first reduces the permanent interest rate, then the temporary interest rate, then
34:1326:108698:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:extends the mortgage term, and finally does principal forbearance. Figure 6b shows that by
34:1327:108788:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:first reducing the permanent rate, HAMP has a marginal cost for small payment reductions
34:1328:108876:16:17:89:523:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that is very close to the cost of principal forgiveness and much larger than the e-cient
34:1329:108964:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:default-minimizing modification, which uses maturity extension first. HAMP Principal Re-
34:1330:109052:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:duction Alternative (PRA), which o-ered principal reduction as the first step in a mortgage
34:1331:109143:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification (see Section 3.1 for details) has an even higher cost from payment reductions.
34:1332:109234:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:The figure shows that HAMP PRA follows the upper envelope of the least e-cient policy
34:1333:109319:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:until a payment reduction of 17 percent is reached. After that, the path of the HAMP PRA
34:1334:109407:17:16:89:317:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:line parallels the standard HAMP modification.
34:1335:109453:16:17:106:523:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In sharp contrast to government-designed HAMP modifications, practitioner-designed
34:1336:109535:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications are much closer to the e-cient frontier. Recall from Section 5.1 that the GSEs
34:1337:109627:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and Chase o-ered most borrowers maturity extension, followed by permanent rate reduction,
34:1338:109716:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:temporary rate reduction (Chase only), and then principal forbearance.49Because the GSEs
34:1339:109804:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and Chase had a specific payment reduction target, we depict them in Figure 6b using dots
34:1340:109893:16:17:89:338:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rather than the lines that we used to depict HAMP.
34:1341:109943:17:16:106:522:281:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f4:A:Potential Gains from More E-cient Modification Design –Our results imply
34:1342:110015:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that modifications in a future crisis can be redesigned to make borrowers, lenders, and tax-
34:1343:110107:17:16:89:523:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payers better o-. To gauge the magnitude of the potential gains, we evaluate our proposed
34:1344:110196:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification structure in comparison to HAMP, where the median borrower received a 38
34:1345:110281:17:16:89:522:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:percent payment reduction. We consider two ways to quantify the potential gains of more
34:1346:110368:16:16:89:196:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:e-cient modifications.
34:1347:110390:16:17:106:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:First, using our “e-cient default-minimizing modification” structure we find that the
34:1348:110475:17:16:89:522:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:same median payment reduction could have been provided at $63,000 lower cost per mod-
34:1349:110560:16:15:98:523:150:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:48Our estimates imply than a lender would break-even by o-ering a payment reduction of 65 percent
34:1350:110657:15:10:89:522:135:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:through a maturity extension to 40 years, a temporary interest rate reduction down to 2 percent, and principal
34:1351:110767:10:11:89:522:125:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:forbearance of 18 percent of the loan balance. Online Appendix Figure 25a shows that when we incorporate
34:1352:110871:11:11:89:522:114:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the social cost of foreclosure of $51,000 from U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (2010),
34:1353:110974:11:11:89:522:103:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:the break-even point for lenders and taxpayers is a payment reduction of 70 percent. Online Appendix Figure
34:1354:111081:11:8:89:504:92:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:25b shows that the same broad patterns hold for payments owed NPV as for expected payments NPV.
34:1355:111176:8:0:98:408:84:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:?:49Chase also o-ered principal forgiveness to some borrowers with high LTVs.
35:1356:111253:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ification to lenders and taxpayers. This is equal to 26 percent of the unpaid balance of a
35:1357:111343:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:typical loan.50Aggregating over all 1.7 million HAMP modifications, this implies a poten-
35:1358:111432:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:tial unnecessary cost of $108 billion. Taxpayers spent around $27 billion subsidizing HAMP
35:1359:111522:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modifications (Government Accountability O-ce 2016). Therefore, our results imply that
35:1360:111608:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP could have been designed with no taxpayer subsidies and a much lower cost to
35:1361:111689:17:16:89:417:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:investors, while maintaining the same amount of payment reduction.
35:1362:111755:16:17:106:523:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Alternatively, if we allocate all the gains from redesigning modifications to reducing
35:1363:111841:17:16:89:522:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrower payments, the same amount of lender and taxpayer cost can be used to achieve
35:1364:111926:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:substantially more default reduction. Again considering the median HAMP borrower, we
35:1365:112010:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:find that an additional 33 percentage points of payment reduction could have been provided
35:1366:112100:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:at the same cost, cutting default rates by one-third. Aggregating over all HAMP modifi-
35:1367:112187:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cations, this implies that 240,000 defaults could have been avoided at no additional cost to
35:1368:112279:17:16:89:188:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:lenders or taxpayers.
35:1369:112300:16:17:106:523:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our proposed approach has benefits beyond improving outcomes for borrowers in a gov-
35:1370:112384:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ernment program.  For example, the potential default reduction would be even larger if
35:1371:112470:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:we considered redesigningallthe 10 million public and private modifications completed in
35:1372:112558:16:17:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the Great Recession. Furthermore, when incorporating the $51,000 social cost of foreclo-
35:1373:112646:17:16:89:522:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sures estimated in U.S. Department of Housing and Urban Development (2010), the default
35:1374:112733:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction just from re-designing HAMP would have generated $6 billion in social value.
35:1375:112819:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Taken together, these results suggest that the gains in a future modification program could
35:1376:112910:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:be divided such that borrowers, lenders and taxpayers all benefit relative to what was im-
35:1377:113000:17:16:89:250:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:plemented in the Great Recession
35:1378:113032:16:16:106:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Another advantage of the e-cient default-minimizing modification is that it is likely to
35:1379:113120:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:generate less ex-ante moral hazard. Some borrowers who did not have a liquidity problem
35:1380:113207:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:may have defaulted on their mortgages in order to become eligible for the generous subsidies.
35:1381:113300:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Mayer et al. (2014) document increased defaults after Countrywide announced a generous
35:1382:113386:17:16:89:522:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:modification program. The Home A-ordable Refinance Program was specifically created
35:1383:113469:16:17:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to allow underwater borrowers to refinance without needing to become delinquent to get
35:1384:113555:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP. Compared to HAMP, a modification with little change in the NPV of payments
35:1385:113635:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:owed may not be attractive to borrowers who are current on their mortgages, and, even if
35:1386:113723:17:22:89:443:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:it is, the resulting modifications will not be costly to lenders or taxpayers.
35:1387:113801:22:26:89:268:193:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f28:C:6.2.3  Ex-ante Mortgage Design
35:1388:113831:26:17:106:523:167:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our empirical results about ex-post debt restructuring also help inform the theoretical
35:1389:113918:17:16:89:522:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:debate about optimal ex-ante mortgage design. A number of recent papers have analyzed
35:1390:114003:16:16:89:522:134:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:alternative mortgage contracts with built-in features designed to assist households overcome
35:1391:114095:16:17:89:522:118:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:periods of financial distress. Eberly and Krishnamurthy (2014) propose a fixed rate mortgage
35:1392:114187:17:15:98:522:101:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:50Although our estimate of the potential value from well-designed modifications is large, it is similar to
35:1393:114293:15:11:89:522:86:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:prior work by Maturana (2017) showing that private modifications raised the NPV of a loan by 16 percent
35:1394:114396:11:0:89:179:75:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:of the unpaid balance.
36:1395:114420:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:(FRM) with a one-time option to convert to an adjustable-rate mortgage (ARM), and Guren
36:1396:114507:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:et al. (2018a) develop an equilibrium model of the housing market to evaluate this contract.
36:1397:114599:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:They find that the option to convert to an ARM is more e-ective than alternative contracts
36:1398:114689:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:because it front-loads the payment reduction to the borrower, and does so at similar cost
36:1399:114778:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to the lender. Our results provide empirical evidence that contracts front-loading payment
36:1400:114868:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reductions to households in financial distress will be more e-ective at preventing defaults
36:1401:114959:16:17:89:522:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:than an alternative contract with equal cost to the lender that spreads payment reductions
36:1402:115049:17:16:89:238:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:throughout the mortgage term.
36:1403:115078:16:16:106:523:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Similarly, we also provide empirical support for proposals specifically contemplating the
36:1404:115167:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:option to extend mortgage maturities. Campbell et al. (2018) compare an ARM with a re-
36:1405:115253:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:finance option to an ARM with the option to temporarily allow for interest-only payments
36:1406:115341:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:with a corresponding increase in its maturity. They find that this maturity extension option
36:1407:115433:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:outperforms a refinance option because it provides similar liquidity-provision benefits to bor-
36:1408:115528:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rowers at much lower cost to lenders. Our results show that immediate payment reduction
36:1409:115615:17:16:89:523:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:can indeed be e-ective at reducing defaults even if structured with o-setting payments in
36:1410:115704:16:28:89:304:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the future so as to minimize costs to lenders.
36:1411:115750:28:30:89:306:434:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:7  Implications: Consumption
36:1412:115778:30:16:106:523:404:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In this section we explore the positive and normative implications of our consumption
36:1413:115863:16:17:89:522:388:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:results.  From a positive perspective, we describe a simple model that clarifies that ac-
36:1414:115952:17:16:89:522:371:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cess to liquidity can explain why the tight link between housing wealth and consumption
36:1415:116039:16:16:89:522:355:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:breaks down for underwater borrowers. We find that collateral constraints drive a wedge
36:1416:116126:16:17:89:522:339:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:between an underwater borrower’s MPC out of cash and their MPC out of housing wealth.
36:1417:116211:17:16:89:522:322:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:From a normative perspective, this implies that payment reduction policies are at least 10
36:1418:116301:16:17:89:523:306:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:times more e-ective than principal reduction at stimulating the consumption of underwater
36:1419:116390:17:23:89:139:289:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers.
36:1420:116400:23:26:89:517:266:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:7.1  Positive: Liquidity Explains Why Principal Reduction is Ine-ective
36:1421:116471:26:16:106:523:240:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In Section 4.3 we showed that our estimated MPC out of housing wealth for underwater
36:1422:116555:16:17:89:522:224:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers is an order of magnitude smaller than the MPC for average borrowers analyzed in
36:1423:116644:17:16:89:522:207:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:prior studies. Furthermore, prior research had shown that highly leveraged (but still above
36:1424:116735:16:17:89:522:191:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:water) borrowers had even higher MPCs, driving arguments in favor of principal reduction
36:1425:116823:17:16:89:351:174:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:as a way to stimulate consumption during a downturn.
36:1426:116875:16:17:106:523:158:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We argue that the inability of underwater borrowers to monetize the wealth gains from
36:1427:116960:17:16:89:522:141:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction can explain why they are far less sensitive to housing wealth changes
36:1428:117049:16:16:89:522:125:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:than borrowers in other economic conditions. In the changes examined in prior research,
36:1429:117136:16:17:89:522:109:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:housing wealth gains expanded borrowers’ credit access. Mian and Sufi (2014a) show that
36:1430:117223:17:16:89:522:92:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:equity withdrawal through increased borrowing can account for the entire e-ect of housing
36:1431:117312:16:0:89:522:76:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:wealth on spending between 2002 and 2006. But if homeowners face a collateral constraint
37:1432:117402:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rather than a “natural” borrowing limit allowing them to monetize the present value of
37:1433:117488:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:their minimum expected lifetime net worth, principal reductions that still leave borrowers
37:1434:117578:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:underwater will not immediately relax this constraint.51Indeed, Defusco (2017) shows
37:1435:117662:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that a significant fraction of the additional borrowing arising from house price gains is due
37:1436:117755:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to relaxing collateral constraints.  If borrowers cannot immediately monetize the wealth
37:1437:117843:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:gained by debt forgiveness, it may not be surprising that they do not respond by increasing
37:1438:117934:16:17:89:160:610:119:g_d0_f4:64:g_d0_f5:B:consumption.52
37:1439:117948:17:16:106:523:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:On the other hand, even if borrowing constraints are not relaxed immediately, it is
37:1440:118031:16:16:89:523:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:possible that forward-looking agents building up a bu-er of assets could respond if they
37:1441:118119:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:believed principal forgiveness would relax their constraints in the near future. We calculate
37:1442:118212:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that since borrowers remained underwater and collateral constraints had tightened, it would
37:1443:118303:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:take eight years before the average principal reduction recipient in HAMP would expect to
37:1444:118392:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:be able to increase borrowing as a result of these principal reductions. A dynamic model of
37:1445:118483:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:household optimization is useful for understanding whether such a lengthy delay can indeed
37:1446:118573:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:explain why borrowers did not increase consumption.  We describe such a model in the
37:1447:118657:16:22:89:210:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:remainder of this section.
37:1448:118683:22:26:89:255:440:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f28:C:7.1.1  Model Setup Summary
37:1449:118709:26:17:106:523:414:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In order to more formally explore whether access to liquidity can explain why the tight
37:1450:118796:17:16:89:522:397:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:link between housing wealth and consumption breaks down for underwater borrowers, we
37:1451:118880:16:17:89:522:381:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:build a partial equilibrium life cycle model of consumption and default. We leave the details
37:1452:118973:17:16:89:432:364:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of the model to the online appendix and discuss the main findings here.
37:1453:119044:16:16:106:523:348:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The model contains one simple addition relative to the standard life-cycle consumption
37:1454:119130:16:17:89:522:332:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:problem in Carroll et al. (2018): households own a home and can only borrow against their
37:1455:119219:17:16:89:522:315:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:home equity subject to a collateral constraint. When households are far underwater, they
37:1456:119307:16:17:89:522:299:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:are far from the point where the collateral constraint will cease to bind. This means that
37:1457:119397:17:16:89:522:282:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:while debt reductions or house price increases raise housing wealth, households are unable
37:1458:119487:16:17:89:522:266:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to monetize this wealth in the near term.  Conversely, when house prices fall and LTVs
37:1459:119573:17:16:89:522:249:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:are pushed beyond the initial collateral constraint, consistent with real-world mortgage
37:1460:119661:16:16:89:522:233:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:contracts we do not assume households are forced to immediately repay excess mortgage
37:1461:119746:16:17:89:522:217:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:debt. This contrasts with the treatment of debt as a one-period bond present in some of
37:1462:119833:17:16:89:522:200:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the prior theoretical literature where forced deleveraging creates a strong link between debt
37:1463:119926:16:17:89:522:184:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:levels and consumption (e.g., Eggertsson and Krugman 2012, Guerrieri and Lorenzoni 2017).
37:1464:120015:17:15:106:523:167:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The full setup is described in online Appendix Section D.1 and the parameterization is
37:1465:120101:15:15:98:522:152:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:51Beraja et al. (2017) document a related channel: underwater borrowers are usually not able to refinance
37:1466:120206:15:7:89:491:137:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:their mortgages. See Carroll (1992) and Aiyagari (1994) for discussions of natural borrowing limits.
37:1467:120306:7:15:98:522:130:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:52The possibility that liquidity can explain the lack of response is also consistent with prior research looking
37:1468:120418:15:11:89:522:115:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:at large price declines. Mian et al. (2013) and Kaplan et al. (2016) both document a non-linearity in the
37:1469:120523:11:11:89:522:104:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:consumption response to house price declines, with a large MPC for small declines but a decreasing MPC for
37:1470:120629:11:11:89:522:93:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:large declines. Mian et al. (2013) suggest that the non-linearity they document could be caused by smaller
37:1471:120735:11:10:89:522:82:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:responses once borrowers become underwater. Similarly, our evidence suggests that for borrowers who start
37:1472:120840:10:0:89:422:72:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:substantially underwater, gains in housing wealth do not a-ect their consumption.
38:1473:120923:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:described in section D.2. In section D.4.1 we show that this simple model can quantitively
38:1474:121013:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:match estimates in the prior literature for the consumption response to housing price changes
38:1475:121106:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of both average and highly leveraged (but above water) households. We now consider its
38:1476:121192:17:22:89:249:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:lessons for underwater borrowers.
38:1477:121225:22:26:89:439:637:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f28:C:7.1.2  Consumption Response to Principal Reduction in Model
38:1478:121284:26:17:106:523:611:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:A reduction in mortgage debt levels a-ects today’s consumption through two channels.
38:1479:121368:17:16:89:522:594:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:The first is a future cash-on-hand e-ect.  Reducing mortgage debt reduces a borrower’s
38:1480:121454:16:17:89:522:578:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:housing payments over time and increases a homeowner’s expected home equity gain when
38:1481:121539:17:16:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:they sell the house. These translate into consumption according to the homeowner’s MPC
38:1482:121625:16:17:89:522:545:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:out of cash-on-hand gains at future dates. The second channel is a collateral e-ect. Reducing
38:1483:121718:17:16:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:debt levels frees up home equity that raises the household’s borrowing limit over time.
38:1484:121805:16:16:89:522:512:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:This change translates into consumption today according to the homeowner’s MPC out of
38:1485:121890:16:17:89:522:496:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:increased collateral in future dates. We show this decomposition formally in online Appendix
38:1486:121982:17:16:89:156:479:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Section D.4.2.
38:1487:121996:16:17:106:523:463:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:This clarifies that the key forces determining the consumption response to debt for-
38:1488:122080:17:16:89:522:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:giveness are the timeline under which debt reductions translate into higher cash-on-hand
38:1489:122168:16:17:89:522:430:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:(through lower payments or through home sale) and increased borrowing capacity, and the
38:1490:122255:17:16:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrower’s MPC out of these future cash-on-hand and future collateral gains. Berger et al.
38:1491:122345:16:17:89:522:397:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:(2018) show that the response to housing wealth gains achieved from increased house prices
38:1492:122435:17:16:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:depends on current home values and the marginal propensity to consume out of wealth. Our
38:1493:122523:16:16:89:522:364:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:analysis adds that the MPC out of wealth gains will depend crucially on a borrower’s initial
38:1494:122615:16:17:89:522:348:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:home equity position. Underwater borrowers receiving a dollar of housing wealth are only
38:1495:122703:17:16:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:able to monetize this gain by borrowing or selling their home once they are above water,
38:1496:122791:16:17:89:522:315:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:which may be far in the future. In this case, the consumption response today will depend
38:1497:122879:17:16:89:471:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:on a household’s MPC out of expected cash or collateral gains far in the future.
38:1498:122959:16:17:106:523:282:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In our model, households are unresponsive to cash or collateral gains far in the future.
38:1499:123047:17:16:89:522:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:To explain why they are unresponsive, it is helpful to divide households into three categories
38:1500:123141:16:16:89:522:249:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:based on their cash-on-hand relative to permanent income. First, households with low cash-
38:1501:123231:16:17:89:522:233:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:on-hand consume all their assets each period. These households are only responsive to cash
38:1502:123321:17:16:89:522:216:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:or collateral they can access today. Second, households with moderate levels of cash-on-hand
38:1503:123413:16:17:89:522:200:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:are building up a bu-er of assets. For these households, near-term cash or collateral reduces
38:1504:123506:17:16:89:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the precautionary value of saving in the current period and increases consumption. However,
38:1505:123597:16:17:89:522:167:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cash or collateral grants several years in the future have no precautionary value and do not
38:1506:123689:17:16:89:523:150:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:a-ect spending. Third, high cash-on-hand households consume only the annuity value of
38:1507:123774:16:16:89:522:134:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cash grants regardless of their timing. We show this visually by plotting the consumption
38:1508:123863:16:17:89:475:118:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:response to future cash and future collateral gains in online Appendix Figure 26.
38:1509:123944:17:16:106:523:101:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The lack of response to future cash and collateral gains can explain why HAMP-type
38:1510:124026:16:0:89:522:85:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction failed to increase consumption. We explore this in the model by consid-
39:1511:124119:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ering the consumption response to principal forgiveness for a household matching the typical
39:1512:124211:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:HAMP borrower. By design, principal reduction in HAMP had no incremental e-ect on
39:1513:124292:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payments relative to alternative modifications until year six, and we find that it would be
39:1514:124383:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:eight years before principal forgiveness translated into increased borrowing capacity.53Since
39:1515:124476:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:no groups of borrowers have strong consumption responses to cash and collateral gains so far
39:1516:124568:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in the future, we find that this can explain why HAMP did not lead to increased spending
39:1517:124656:16:17:89:174:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in the short term.
39:1518:124674:17:16:106:523:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:This can be seen visually in Figure 7a, which shows the consumption function out of
39:1519:124757:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:increasing amounts of principal reduction for borrowers starting at an LTV of 150 (the
39:1520:124843:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:median LTV for HAMP principal reduction recipients).  It shows that the consumption
39:1521:124926:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:function out of home equity gains is S-shaped, convex in a small region below the collateral
39:1522:125018:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:constraint, and concave above it. Borrowers are insensitive to principal reductions until such
39:1523:125112:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reductions bring them close to their constraint. Principal reduction for deeply underwater
39:1524:125202:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers does not relax current constraints and has little precautionary value, hence con-
39:1525:125293:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sumption is una-ected. In online Appendix Section D.4.4 we show quantitatively that the
39:1526:125380:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:MPC out of HAMP-like principal reduction is close to zero under a variety of alternative
39:1527:125468:16:17:89:177:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:parameterizations.
39:1528:125486:17:16:106:523:429:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our result contrasts with debt overhang models in which forced deleveraging leads to
39:1529:125570:16:17:89:522:413:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:depressed consumption.  For example, in Eggertsson and Krugman (2012) and Guerrieri
39:1530:125653:17:16:89:522:396:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:and Lorenzoni (2017), debt is modeled as a one-period bond. In this setting, when a credit
39:1531:125743:16:17:89:522:380:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:crunch reduces the borrowing limit, borrowers who find themselves beyond the borrowing
39:1532:125829:17:16:89:522:363:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:constraint are forced to immediately cut consumption in order to delever. Applying this
39:1533:125916:16:16:89:522:347:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:assumption to the mortgage setting implies that when housing prices fall such that the LTV
39:1534:126006:16:17:89:522:331:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ratio becomes greater than 100, borrowers need to immediately repay their outstanding debt
39:1535:126096:17:16:89:522:314:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:until they are above water. Under this hypothetical scenario, borrowers receiving principal
39:1536:126187:16:17:89:522:298:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction would see immediate decreases in the amount of forced repayment.  Principal
39:1537:126272:17:16:89:405:281:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:reduction would increase consumption by reducing debt overhang.
39:1538:126335:16:17:106:523:265:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:But in practice, as in our model, mortgages in particular are long-term loans. Nothing
39:1539:126421:17:16:89:522:248:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:forces borrowers to immediately delever when they are far underwater. Modeling housing
39:1540:126507:16:17:89:522:232:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:debt as a long-term contract removes a mechanical link between debt levels and consumption
39:1541:126597:17:16:89:523:215:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:present in some of the prior literature, and reduces the expected e-ectiveness of mortgage
39:1542:126687:16:16:89:522:199:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:debt reduction policies.  Other recent papers to consider the e-ect of debt and housing
39:1543:126774:16:17:89:522:183:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:wealth in settings with long-term contracts include Berger et al. (2018), Chen et al. (2013),
39:1544:126867:17:16:89:327:166:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Kaplan et al. (2017), and Justiniano et al. (2015).
39:1545:126918:16:15:98:522:150:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:53This eight years estimate is based on the HAMP mortgage contract, which left borrowers underwater
39:1546:127017:15:11:89:522:135:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:with a median LTV ratio after modification of 114, an assumption that homeowners can only borrow up to
39:1547:127119:11:11:89:522:124:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:80% of the value of their home in this time period, and an assumption of 1% real annual house price growth
39:1548:127225:11:11:89:522:113:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:based on contemporaneous futures contracts. See online Appendix D.4.3 for details supporting the second
39:1549:127328:11:0:89:178:102:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:and third assumption.
40:1550:127351:0:27:89:509:709:119:g_d0_f28:119:g_d0_f28:C:7.1.3  Wedge Between MPC Out of Housing Wealth and MPC Out of Cash
40:1551:127417:27:16:106:523:682:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:The inability to monetize housing wealth drives a wedge between an underwater bor-
40:1552:127499:16:17:89:522:666:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:rower’s marginal propensity to consume out of cash and their marginal propensity to con-
40:1553:127587:17:16:89:522:649:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sume out of housing wealth.  This can be observed visually in Figure 7b.  In this figure
40:1554:127675:16:17:89:522:633:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:we take low-cash-on-hand borrowers at various LTV levels and plot the MPC out of $1 of
40:1555:127761:17:16:89:522:616:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cash or $1 of housing wealth gained by principal reduction. As in the empirical results in
40:1556:127851:16:16:89:522:600:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Mian et al. (2013), borrowers near their collateral constraint have a high MPC out of hous-
40:1557:127942:16:17:89:522:584:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ing wealth gains. However, borrowers far underwater are unresponsive to housing wealth
40:1558:128028:17:16:89:522:567:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:changes even though they are highly responsive to cash transfers. This highlights one way
40:1559:128117:16:17:89:522:551:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that housing wealth is special. Because it can only be monetized when borrowers have pos-
40:1560:128206:17:16:89:522:534:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:itive home equity above a collateral constraint, borrowers respond less to housing wealth
40:1561:128295:16:23:89:219:518:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:gains than they do to cash.
40:1562:128322:23:26:89:458:495:143:g_d0_f3:143:g_d0_f3:C:7.2  Normative: Designing Policies to Stimulate Consumption
40:1563:128381:26:17:106:523:469:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Our wedge result implies that high leverage is a bad “tag” for targeting policies that
40:1564:128467:17:16:89:522:452:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:increase housing wealth, even though it is a good “tag” for targeting policies trying to
40:1565:128555:16:17:89:522:436:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:provide cash to borrowers with high MPCs. Our empirical and theoretical results show that
40:1566:128644:17:16:89:522:419:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:principal reduction will fail to stimulate consumption for underwater borrowers. However,
40:1567:128733:16:17:89:522:403:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:our model suggests that low-wealth, underwater borrowers would have an MPC out of cash
40:1568:128819:17:16:89:522:386:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:around 30 cents. This high MPC is qualitatively consistent with the sensitivity of spending
40:1569:128910:16:16:89:522:370:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:to payment reduction from our event study graphs in Figure 3a. It is also quantitatively
40:1570:128998:16:17:89:522:354:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:consistent with DiMaggio et al. (2017) who find that underwater borrowers have MPCs out
40:1571:129085:17:16:89:391:337:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:of cash more than twice as high as non-underwater households.
40:1572:129146:16:17:106:523:321:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:We find that payment reduction is substantially more cost e-ective than principal re-
40:1573:129231:17:16:89:522:304:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:duction at stabilizing consumption. The government spent an average of $0.30 to subsidize
40:1574:129320:16:17:89:522:288:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:each dollar of principal forgiveness in HAMP, for a total government cost of $4.6 billion.
40:1575:129410:17:16:89:522:271:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Our model suggests that if the same amount of money had been spent on direct transfers to
40:1576:129499:16:16:89:522:255:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:borrowers, the partial equilibrium spending increase would have been $1.4 billion–ten times
40:1577:129590:16:17:89:522:239:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:more than even the upper bound of our estimates for the consumption response to prin-
40:1578:129675:17:16:89:522:222:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:cipal forgiveness would suggest. Policies seeking to raise aggregate demand by increasing
40:1579:129764:16:17:89:522:206:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the housing wealth of leveraged borrowers will be ine-ective precisely when policymakers
40:1580:129852:17:16:89:522:189:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:might otherwise want to use them, i.e., in times when many borrowers are underwater and
40:1581:129939:16:17:89:265:173:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:collateral constraints have tightened.
40:1582:129977:17:16:106:522:156:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:This finding reinforces the conclusions in Section 6.2.2 about e-cient modification de-
40:1583:130064:16:16:89:522:140:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sign. That section focused on the default-reduction gains from maximizing immediate pay-
40:1584:130152:16:17:89:522:124:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:ment reduction for a given amount of lender and taxpayer cost. Our results here imply that
40:1585:130242:17:16:89:422:107:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:the same structure would also maximize immediate demand stimulus.
40:1586:130307:16:17:106:522:91:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Although principal reduction as implemented during the crisis is an ine-ective way to
40:1587:130392:17:0:89:523:74:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:provide immediate stimulus, it is possible for principal reduction policies to a-ect consump-
41:1588:130487:0:17:89:522:709:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:tion.  We consider two cases.  First, although we show that principal reduction has no
41:1589:130573:17:16:89:522:692:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:immediate e-ect on consumption, in the long-term principal reduction translates into lower
41:1590:130663:16:17:89:522:676:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:payments and increased borrowing capacity and hence should eventually a-ect consumption.
41:1591:130751:17:16:89:522:659:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:Although we cannot analyze this e-ect empirically within our sample window, our model
41:1592:130836:16:17:89:522:643:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:shows that consumption would likely begin responding about five years after modification
41:1593:130924:17:16:89:522:626:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:for the average borrower. To the extent that principal reductions were pursued for short-run
41:1594:131016:16:17:89:505:610:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:macroeconomic stabilization, long-run consumption responses will have limited benefit.
41:1595:131102:17:16:106:523:593:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Second, more generous principal reductions that did push borrowers above their col-
41:1596:131185:16:16:89:522:577:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:lateral constraint might have led to some immediate consumption response. However, this
41:1597:131272:16:17:89:522:561:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:would have been an ine-cient way to raise consumption. Figure 7 shows that all of the
41:1598:131357:17:16:89:522:544:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:consumption increase is coming from the region near the collateral constraint. This means
41:1599:131446:16:17:89:522:528:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:that a policy of targeting deeply underwater borrowers with more generous writedowns will
41:1600:131535:17:16:89:522:511:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:expend substantial resources in a region with no stimulative e-ect.54This also points to a
41:1601:131625:16:17:89:522:495:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:limitation of one of Fisher’s policy recommendations for reversing “debt deflations” (Fisher
41:1602:131717:17:16:89:522:478:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:1933). He suggests reflating asset prices. Our results suggest that this may be ine-ective
41:1603:131807:16:16:89:522:462:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:at increasing demand for those who are underwater unless pursued aggressively enough to
41:1604:131894:16:28:89:239:446:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:bring them into positive equity.
41:1605:131926:28:30:89:190:418:206:g_d0_f3:206:g_d0_f3:C:8  Conclusion
41:1606:131939:30:17:106:522:388:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:In this paper, we explore how borrower liquidity and wealth a-ect default and consump-
41:1607:132025:17:16:89:522:371:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:tion decisions through the lens of mortgage modifications in the Great Recession. Using
41:1608:132112:16:16:89:522:355:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:quasi-experimental research designs, we show principal reduction that leaves current mort-
41:1609:132202:16:17:89:522:339:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:gage payments unchanged–wealth without liquidity–has no detectable e-ect on default or
41:1610:132288:17:16:89:522:322:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:consumption. In sharp contrast, we find that immediate payment reduction with no change
41:1611:132375:16:17:89:522:306:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:in the net present value of payments owed–liquidity without wealth–significantly reduces
41:1612:132463:17:16:89:125:289:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:default.
41:1613:132471:16:17:106:523:273:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:A:Taken together, these results suggest that liquidity is the key driver of borrower con-
41:1614:132558:17:16:89:522:256:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:sumption and default decisions. Changes in housing debt are irrelevant for the consumption
41:1615:132648:16:17:89:522:240:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:decisions of underwater borrowers because they are unable to access this wealth. From a
41:1616:132735:17:16:89:522:223:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:policy perspective, we show that distressed debt modifications can be redesigned with sub-
41:1617:132825:16:16:89:522:207:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:stantial potential gains. Applied to the main government program for distressed borrowers
41:1618:132914:16:17:89:522:191:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:during the Great Recession, our results imply that 240,000 defaults could have been avoided
41:1619:133005:17:77:89:312:174:119:g_d0_f4:119:g_d0_f4:B:at no additional cost to investors or taxpayers.
41:1620:133053:77:15:98:522:97:36:g_d0_f7:80:g_d0_f8:F:54One implication of this result is that a principal reduction policy very early in the crisis before credit
41:1621:133161:15:10:89:522:82:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:supply had tightened and before price declines had pushed borrowers into negative equity might have had a
41:1622:133266:10:0:89:213:72:80:g_d0_f8:80:g_d0_f8:F:positive e-ect on consumption.
